Britain Emphasizes Aviation

[London] Parliamentary Secretary to the Air Ministry Sassoon declared firmly in the House of Commons today that commercial air transport is not only valuable for its speed, but also seeks its stability and comfort. Although French aircraft on the London-Paris route are faster than British aircraft, Imperial Airways carries three times as many passengers as France. The number of French airline passengers has decreased by 30 percent. The subsidies paid by the British government to Imperial Airways are far less than those paid by the United States, France, Germany, and Italy. The reason is mainly that the purpose of the subsidies is to develop air transport on a solid commercial basis, and there is no other intention. In the future, the British government will conclude a contract with Imperial Airways, which will stipulate minimum speed conditions. Concrete plans to increase the speed of aviation affairs between London and other cities in the Empire have been considered for months, but he cannot announce them at present. (Reuters dispatch on the 1st)

British Aviators Create New Record Again

Flying from Melbourne Back to London

The British aviators Lindbergh Reece and Waller landed here at 1:15 pm today, breaking all round-trip speed records from London to Melbourne. The two aviators' final leg was a long flight from Athens to here. The aircraft they used was the one that had flown from London to Melbourne earlier. Their round-trip record time was 13 days, 6 hours, and 39 minutes. The two aviators previously set a new record of 6 days, 15 hours, and 39 minutes from London to Melbourne, ranking fourth in the previous London to Melbourne flight race. (National dispatch on the 2nd)

(Denchu dispatch on the 2nd)

Anglo-German Payment Agreement

British Minister Announces to Parliament

[London] The Secretary of Commerce, Mr. Runciman, announced in the House of Commons today that the Anglo-German debt dispute has been resolved with an agreement. According to the agreement, Germany guarantees to purchase British goods with 55% of the proceeds from German exports to Britain. The German National Bank will also immediately allocate £400,000 to settle outstanding debts to Britain. Discussions for the Anglo-German financial and trade agreement began in earnest after Sir Frederick Leith-Ross, the British government's chief economic advisor, arrived in Germany on September 19th, and have gradually progressed. Leith-Ross's mission to Germany had two objectives: first, to find a way for Germany to settle commercial debts of approximately £2 million; and second, to find a way for Germany to guarantee future payments for British goods purchased. Since September 24th, all of Germany's foreign trade has required government approval. British yarn merchants subsequently used a cessation of exports to Germany as a form of resistance. Eighteen textile factories in Germany even moved to Britain this autumn because they had no yarn to spin, so the current agreement is, to a great extent, Germany's only option. (1st National Telegram)

[Berlin] Anglo-German debt and trade negotiations were completed today. The agreement reached will be named the "Payment Treaty," and the remaining clauses are as follows: "(1) Germany designates 55% of the value of its exports to be deposited in Britain to pay for the price of British goods entering Germany. (2) Germany issues foreign currency securities to pay for British goods entering Germany. If, after a one-month trial, practical difficulties are encountered, Germany may consult with Britain to amend this. Furthermore, Germany will not restrict the import of British coal, coke, cotton yarn, cotton fabrics, etc. (3) Germany agrees to pay Britain £400,000 in cash upon signing the treaty to settle the second phase of old debts. (4) The British side collects German accounts to prepare for the settlement of German old debts. (5) Within one year, Germany should deposit in Britain the remaining 45% of the value of its exports to Britain to settle the remaining debts owed to Britain. (6) Germany should pay in full the interest on the Dawes and Young bonds owed to British citizens. (7) If this treaty is violated, the Clearing Office will act as agent. This treaty may be cancelled by either party with one month's notice to the other party." (1st National Telegram)

Another Typhoon Hits the Tokyo Area

[Tokyo] Tokyo and the surrounding areas were suddenly struck by a typhoon and heavy rain last night, causing minor damage, but some houses were flooded. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

U.S. Secretary of State Announces the Abandonment of High Tariff Policies

Moving Towards Free International Trade

[New York] At today's meeting of the National Foreign Trade Council, a letter from Secretary of State Hull was read, stating that the United States is now prepared to abolish its previous high-tariff policies and move towards a more liberal international trade path. The United States now invites other countries to join the effort to eliminate the harm of high tariffs. The impact of the 1930 tariff act has only caused countries to close their doors and reject American goods. We now acknowledge that exports paid for with loans are merely gifts to foreign countries. At the same time, President Roosevelt has sent a telegram to Mr. Farrell, the chairman of the National Foreign Trade Council, stating that we now want to find ways to restore international trade that benefit all countries, not just one. One of the biggest causes of commercial stagnation is the artificial barriers that hinder the exchange of goods. (1st Reuters Telegram)

U.S. Treasury Deficit of 100 Million Yuan

Sharp Increase in Gold Imports

[Washington] The Treasury Department announced today that the financial deficit for this fiscal year has reached a huge sum of 100 million yuan. The government's total revenue is 1,208,184,666 yuan, while expenditures are 2,234,973,664 yuan, resulting in a deficit of 1,026,788,998 yuan. The deficit for the same period last year was only 481,906,629 yuan. Revenue is approximately 10,000,000 yuan less than the budget. (1st National Telegram)

[Washington] The U.S. government deficit for this fiscal year exceeds 1,000,000,000 U.S. dollars. It was learned today that expenditures exceed income by a total of 1,026,788,000 U.S. dollars. Gold revenue exceeds 2,000,000 U.S. dollars, bringing the total value of gold stored in the Treasury to 8,001,062,000 U.S. dollars. The Treasury's gold value exceeding 8,000,000,000 U.S. dollars is a first. Emergency expenditures for this fiscal year total 1,105,872,000 U.S. dollars, and regular expenditures total 1,129,101,000 U.S. dollars. Revenue totals 1,208,184,000 U.S. dollars. The number of silver certificates issued this fiscal year to pay for silver purchased by the Treasury under the Silver Purchase Act has increased, exceeding 500,000,000 U.S. dollars, which is due to the issuance of silver certificates to offset the value of silver previously stored in the U.S. Treasury. (1st Reuters Telegram)

[Washington] According to today's gazette, gold imports to the United States increased sharply in October compared to September. Gold imports in October were valued at 6,850,000 U.S. dollars, while in September they were 15,600 U.S. dollars. (1st National Telegram)

[New York] The U.S. National Foreign Trade Council met here today. Mr. Li, the president of the New York Chinese Chamber of Commerce, said in a speech that China has no preconceived notions about the level of silver prices, but opposes price fluctuations, which make China's foreign exchange rates as volatile as a football being kicked around. In previous years, China opposed the world abandoning silver for gold, and now opposes restoring silver. The reason for both is that China's foreign trade does not suffer losses due to unstable silver prices. Currently, China's silver export tax has the same effect as prohibiting exports. However, it is hoped that after the situation improves in the future, China will not need to control its exchange rates like other countries. Secretary of State Hull also gave a speech, stating that domestic unemployment can only be reduced and the previous standard of living can only be restored after American exports are unhindered. (1st National Telegram)

The Fuxing Maru, Baikal Maru, and four other ships heading to the scene to provide assistance were expected to arrive at the scene at 4:00 PM.

French Military Threat to the Saar; Germany Sees Danger as Playing with Fire

All Germans See French Action as a Challenge to Germany

German Press Warns Britain to Share Responsibility

Britain Expresses Caution on the Saar Issue

[Berlin] The news that France is preparing to send troops to the Saar border to prevent German interference in the election has aroused deep resentment throughout Germany. The German press firmly denies that the National Socialist Party intends to cause trouble in the Saar and accuses France of aiming to manipulate the upcoming plebiscite. The German press hopes that Britain will resolutely refuse to participate in any invasion of the Saar. An unofficial diplomatic dispatch warns Britain that if France sends troops into the Saar, Britain should also be responsible for the consequences. The Council of the League of Nations is scheduled to meet on November 21st to study the issue of the Saar plebiscite.

According to responsible sources in Paris, if Mr. Knox, the chairman of the Saar Governing Commission appointed by the League of Nations, issues a warning stating that the local constabulary cannot restrain the activities of the National Socialist Party, then the motorized units of the French army stationed in the Alsace region can immediately enter the Saar. It is estimated that several thousand soldiers could control the situation within half a day. However, France has no intention of using force. This warning is issued to eliminate the need to use force. Even if troops are deployed, they will not be used to manipulate the vote. Once order is restored, the deployed troops must be withdrawn. The above are the opinions of people in Paris.

A key figure in Berlin expressed his opinion to a Reuters reporter, saying that France is currently playing with fire. If powerful forces attempt to use their military force to influence the plebiscite on January 13th, then the peace and order of the Saar cannot be maintained under any circumstances. Today's editorial in a German government newspaper indirectly criticizes the Saar Governing Commission for biased behavior, saying that France is now preparing to occupy the Saar with force whenever the Governing Commission deems it feasible. However, no matter what the reason, occupying the Saar is an act of defiance against Germany and an act of seizing land under the administration of the League of Nations. The world will condemn it, and those who tolerate such actions will not escape blame.

At the same time, French newspapers are spreading rumors about how strong the German military is. According to one French newspaper, the German military next spring will be even larger than the German military during World War I in 1924. Le Matin in Paris states that the German army numerically outnumbers the French army. Behind Hitler are two million fully armed soldiers with tanks, heavy artillery, and aircraft. As war rumors increase, the French people fear air raids because air forces are the most terrifying of the lethal weapons for killing and destroying houses invented after the Great War. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

[London] The British government is closely monitoring the maintenance of order during the Saar plebiscite and the threat of French military intervention. As a signatory to the Treaty of Versailles, the British government is deeply concerned that the plebiscite be held fairly and without any pressure and believes that the League of Nations is now taking appropriate precautions to ensure the realization of this goal. France's attitude is certainly good, but the British government believes that if all parties in the Saar do not lose their sense of responsibility, France's concerns may not materialize. At the same time, Britain does not want to take any special actions at present. (2nd Reuters Telegram)

War Zone Clearing Committee Established

To Receive the Eastern Tombs on the 15th

The Puppet Police Force at Gubeikou Withdraws

Beiping Correspondence: The War Zone Clearing Committee held its inaugural meeting at 9:00 AM today (the 1st) in the east building of the Political Readjustment Committee. Committee members Li Zeyi, Yin Tong, Yin Rugeng, Zhu Shiqin, Tao Shangming, Yue Kaixian, and Xu Tongxin attended. No ceremony was held. Huang Fu delivered a training speech, stating that the purpose of the committee's establishment is to handle unfinished matters in the war zone and that he hopes that all committee members will adhere to the principle of "speaking less and doing more" and work diligently for the public to gradually achieve the major goals of rectifying officialdom, maintaining public security, restoring the countryside, and completing construction. After the meeting, the committee held its first meeting and passed the committee's operating guidelines. The meeting was adjourned, and a second meeting is scheduled to continue at 9:00 AM tomorrow (the 2nd) to discuss the allocation of work and the direction of various matters. If the meeting cannot be concluded, it will continue on the 3rd. The committee will begin to resolve war zone issues within four to five days.

Regarding the Eastern Tombs issue, it has been decided that the Clearing Committee will formally take over on the 15th of this month. The entry of the newly formed security team into the war zone and other trivial matters are scheduled to be completed within six months.

After negotiations between the Jili-Miyun District Office and the Japanese side, it was agreed that the puppet "National Border Police Force" at Gubeikou South Tianmen Caojialu would withdraw beyond the border after our side provided a discretionary amount for house repair expenses. A portion of the puppet police force, approximately 30 to 40 people, remained in Gubeikou South Pass because the houses outside the pass had not been completely repaired. Now that the Japanese army is building houses at Erdaoqiao, two miles north of the Great Wall, the 30 to 40 puppet police officers in South Pass completely withdrew from the 16th of last month until yesterday. However, there are still four puppet police officers in North Pass who inspect departing passengers. (1st)

International Commercial Telegram

November 2nd Reuters Special Commodity Market Telegram

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: The London gold market opened this morning at 139 shillings and 9 pence, down 1 pence.

London Silver Bar: The London silver price rose 125 today. Spot price is 23 pence and 625, and futures price is 23 pence and 75. Speculators bought in the morning, and China sold. Trading was light, and the closing sentiment was still stable.

Bombay Silver Bar: The Bombay silver market soared today. The spot price rose 8 annas at 11:00 AM and rose again at 5:30 PM to 64 rupees and 15 annas. After the price increase, the market stabilized.

Exchange Rates

Anglo-American: The Anglo-American exchange rate opened at 4 yuan, 9 jiao, and 8 and a half fen, half a fen higher than yesterday's closing exchange rate. At 11:00 AM, it fell 1875 to 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 8 fen, 3 li, and 1 hao, and this price remained unchanged until 2:00 PM.

Anglo-French: The Anglo-French exchange rate opened at 75 francs and 71 centimes, up 12 points. At 11:00 AM, it fell 6 points to 75 francs and 65 centimes, and remained unchanged until 2:00 PM.

American-British: The New York foreign exchange market was sluggish this morning. The American-British exchange rate opened at 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 8 fen, 3 li, 7 hao, and 5 si, 1875 higher, but soon fell 375, the same as yesterday's price. The most recent price is still 4 yuan, 9 jiao, and 8 fen.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: American farmers advocate reducing import barriers rather than suppressing prices to revitalize American exports. Secretary of State Hull also proposed to support this policy, which had a positive impact on the cotton market this morning, with prices rising by about 7 points. Activity in the near-term was not expected at the opening, but trading firms bought in the morning, and brokers also made some purchases, so the near-term received support. Critics expressed the opinion that a kind of restriction is necessary, but it should be done separately from the Peng Hai case. However, some also said that the existing contracts allow contractors to grow at least 25 percent more cotton than allowed in 1934.

Indian Cotton: The Bombay cotton market fell 75 this morning due to long position liquidation and sales by Japanese merchants. The price fell again at 5:30 PM. The April-May period white cotton price was 208 rupees, 1 rupee lower than yesterday's closing.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was quiet today. At 1:00 PM, the January price was 6.50, showing no change. The market was stable due to slight buying from the East.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market rose 375 in the afternoon for the December period, with the price at 4 shillings, 11 pence, and 625, due to insect pests in South Australia and the strong position of the American spot market.

American Wheat: Chicago wheat futures opened this morning up more than 1 cent due to the strong position of the spot market and reports of insect pests in South Australia. Trading was quite active within the first hour after the opening due to purchases by trading firms.

Rubber

London Rubber: There was a definite turnaround in London rubber today, contrary to the trend of the past few days. The price at noon was 6 pence and 6875, up 3125. The rise was due to good news in the market about export restrictions in January next year. Some parties expect a reduction of 30 percent, for a period of three or six months. Others say it will be gradually reduced, first by 27.5 percent for three months and then by 32.5 percent for the next three months. The Rubber Committee is scheduled to convene on November 7th, and the results of its meeting are of great interest to people in the rubber industry.

New York: The New York rubber market opened this morning, showing sympathy for the London market, up 47 points. The market price continued to rise in the morning, with a very stable sentiment and a strong position.

Securities

Gold worth two million US dollars in New York and Paris was shipped to the United States, and more is expected to be shipped, causing gold coins to weaken. This morning, people in the New York securities market were paying close attention to this. The factors favoring the market before the opening included: (1) important long positions were closed, but there was still a lack of impetus, and (2) Ford's business report attracted general attention, but it did not have much impact on the market. The unfavorable factors for the market situation included: (1) railway stocks were under pressure, and (2) government bonds were weak. The securities market opened stably this morning, and although there was not much rise, it seemed to have improved slightly. However, a sustained upward trend is not guaranteed at the moment. The Current Situation in Japan Before and After the Opening of the London Naval Preparatory Conference (Japanese Communication)

Concentrating Political Forces, Mobilizing National Public Opinion

Opening the Door to Britain, No Concessions to the United States

At the first meeting of the London Naval Preparatory Conference, the most important thing was for Britain and the United States to reach an understanding first, and then seek a compromise between Britain, the United States, and Japan. If conference diplomacy prevails, the confrontation between Britain and the United States will not be too sharp, as in the past Washington Conference in 1922. An understanding between Britain and the United States is possible. However, the current global economic panic has not truly reached its bottom. The reason why Britain is struggling to support itself and maintain market prosperity is, firstly, that it relies on its vast colonies and self-governing territories to vigorously implement the economic alliance within the British Empire, and secondly, that Britain took the lead in abandoning the gold standard, stabilizing its markets in South America and Europe.

However, the United States is still Britain's biggest economic rival. The competition between North and South America cannot be eased, and it has no room for mediation in the opposition between European and Asian markets. In addition, the competition for oil and the competition in heavy industry have affected diplomatic relations and naval forces, which have serious foreign characteristics. Japan has done a lot of research on this and knows that Britain and the United States will never reach an understanding on naval disarmament unless they have no other choice, and they cannot unite against Japan. Therefore, when the preparatory conference first opened in June of this year, Britain sent the Prime Minister and the Naval Minister, while the United States sent Davis, a skilled diplomat from the Democratic Party who was familiar with the situation in Europe but did not hold the title of Ambassador, to engage in future disarmament negotiations. However, Japan did not send any important officials at the time, and even the people sent by the Navy were slow to act. Until the British-American consultations stalled, Japan was still using ordinary diplomatic methods to deal with the situation.

On the surface, it seems that Japan was not prepared to respond to the naval preparatory conference with an active approach, and was clinging to its isolated diplomacy. But in fact, this was not the case. It understood that an understanding between Britain and the United States would not succeed, or at least would be difficult to achieve. It still had room to plan, so it specially summoned the ambassadors to the United States, France, and Italy back to the country to prepare for a total diplomatic mobilization. At the same time, the general public in the country was probably indulging in entertainment in the cities, and even if strong stimulants were injected, the reaction was still very small. Moreover, the spread of left-leaning ideas was very frightening. As for the capitalists, they tried their best to seek the safety of investment and were unwilling to take more risks. Therefore, the tune of the extraordinary period, even if sung loudly, was not very realistic after all. It was not easy to deal with both the army and the navy. Moreover, issuing public bonds and advocating an extraordinary period were not permanent solutions after all. Therefore, it wanted to stimulate its people, mobilize national public opinion, and promote the so-called national unity, uniting all parties under the leadership of the military to attend the arms reduction conference.

If Britain and the United States really unite to share the hegemony of the Pacific Ocean, then Japan's position will be very difficult. However, Britain and Japan have had an alliance relationship in the past, and there is still a possibility of understanding in politics now. There are many places where they need each other, and there are also many occasions for mutual use. The difficulty lies in the economic competition, especially in the cotton market, which is Britain's only real rival. Britain will never easily make concessions on this issue, and Japan also sees it as a matter of life and death for its industrial circles, and will fight to the death to compete. However, there is plenty of antagonism between them. If this antagonism is allowed to expand, then the political understanding between the United States and Japan will become illusory. On the eve of the arms reduction conference, Japan is of course particularly vigilant. It uses "open door" as bait to lure Britain, seeking temporary economic benefits in exchange for political understanding at the naval disarmament conference. If Japan's demand for naval equality is agreed to by Britain, then Japan's claim can be continued.

The opposition of the United States is of course to be expected. However, after the British-Japanese understanding, the situation on the conference table will be different. If Japan's proposal is established, then the principle of equality will be confirmed. Either Britain and the United States reduce their current strength, or Japan expands its armaments. This is in line with military requirements and is beneficial to Japan. Otherwise, the conference will break down. According to Japan's wishes, the United States is responsible for the breakdown. Future arms races also seem to be initiated by the United States. Whether in international diplomacy or to the domestic people, Japan can cleverly explain this and forge its plan for military expansion. (October 25, Tokyo)

Northwest Inspection Notes

— Special Correspondent Geng Ya

A Tragedy of Selling Children in Disguise

Weidiebao is a large town in Linze (Fu Yi) County. The residents used to have more than 1,000 households. After repeated wars and disasters, the old died, the strong fled, and now there are only 600 or 700 households. The grain tax of the escaped households is borne by the households that have not escaped, so the suffering is even deeper, and more and more people continue to flee. In recent years, the drought has meant that cultivation is only 50% of normal, so although the county seat is adjacent to areas with a good harvest, the prices in the fort have not fallen. Farmers lack funds and are unable to sow. Even if they offer free labor, no one dares to respond. Therefore, although the year of the great drought in Longxi has passed, the hidden pain felt by the farmers is still increasing. It is still common to see the tragedy of women under the age of 20 being sold to others as wives, maids, or child brides for a standard price of one yuan per year, and I am afraid that this is not unique to one place.

I was strolling outside the Cheshupu Inn in the evening when I suddenly heard a painful cry coming from an alley. I went to see what was happening and saw a man over 40 years old dragging a girl by the foot, scraping her along the ground. There was also a younger boy carrying a pair of red cloth shoes, crying and following along. I quickly stopped him and asked what was going on. I learned that the girl was already a child bride, but she had run away because of abuse and did not want to return. Her father was now forcing her to go back. The girl was only 14 years old, and I couldn't bear to see her like this, so I asked her father to postpone sending her back. He replied, "A married daughter is like a cow or horse that has been sold. What's there to say? Besides, I used two silver dollars and two shi of wheat from her father-in-law a few days ago. Alas, this little thief doesn't even try to earn face for her parents!" I asked, "Did you just give your daughter away after receiving this little bit of silver and wheat?" He replied, "No, I received 14 silver dollars from them before, because she is only 14 years old." At this time, the girl was still crying with her head in her hands. After much persuasion, she finally agreed to return, but she did not want her father to send her, but wanted her uncle to send her. However, according to her father, her uncle had already rejected her request. The reporter was willing to persuade him to go, and the boy carrying the shoes (the girl's brother) led me to her home. Her uncle replied angrily, "I won't send her. Let him (referring to the girl's father) beat her and send her himself. At that time, my sister (referring to the girl's mother) and I said that even if we had to beg for food, we would not want to give our daughter to someone as a child bride. Who told him not to listen?" A woman suddenly turned out from behind the door, her clothes ragged and her face full of tears. She seemed to want to say something, but she couldn't cry out. I asked her and learned that she was the girl's mother. In the end, she said hesitatingly, "Uncle, for the sake of this old boss (referring to the reporter), please send her back one more time." He finally agreed to go to the girl's place, ordered her to go back and wash up, and only when the sun was setting and her uncle urged her did the girl reluctantly come out of the house, tearfully departing. Later, her father, wanting to explain the reason for his cruel sale of his daughter, took out a stack of old and new slips of paper and said, "Commissioner (also called reporter), I am not afraid that you will harm us. Please take a look at these things, and you will understand our suffering." I took the slips and saw that they were all donation notices about three inches long and eight fen wide, with a total of 27 slips in one year. Each slip also had several donation items written on it. In addition to the fixed amount of surcharges on land taxes every year, and the maintenance of local security by the stationed troops, with the people enjoying the right to protection, and the establishment of supply depots to provide grain and miscellaneous supplies not included, there were also "fines for tobacco land" for which donation notices had already arrived before the tobacco had been sown. Farmers were not merchants and had no buying or selling to speak of, except for the tragedy of selling sons and daughters. There was also the "stamp tax donation" that had to be paid monthly (each county in Longxi should pay 300 to 500 stamp tax per month, but Linze is a poor county and pays 160 yuan per month. The county government obtains tax tickets from the provincial bureau and distributes them to various districts and townships regardless of whether the farmers use them or not. The farmers have already paid the stamp tax monthly, but when they need to use marriage certificates, land deeds, etc. and should affix stamps, they have to prepare cash again and buy them from places where stamps are stockpiled, which is also inexplicable), "welcome and hospitality fees" for officials from certain agencies (from the Financial Department and the court to the county government bureau districts) who came to collect money, and "temporary miscellaneous fees" such as gifts, telegrams, subsidies, and photographs for the establishment of certain associations or institutes (although taking photos is a small matter, photographers in remote counties and townships set very high prices, such as at least 12 yuan or 16 yuan for an 8-inch or 12-inch photo, plus the parties involved taking the opportunity to extort, so one notice could cost at least one Yuan head from hundreds of households), and "divine donations and ghost taxes" for welcoming gods and holding temple fairs and praying for rain or clearing skies (this is because among the donation notices, there are several items such as "publicly agreed to offer a fairy maiden opera for ten days, half a unit should pay 12,000 wen, 5 jin of dry noodles," "each unit is publicly assigned four lamps and stoves (?), one lamp planter for one day, bring clear oil," "publicly agreed to set up an altar in the small temple to pray for rain, each unit should pay 6,000 wen for incense, each sincerely offer clear oil and dry noodles," so they are named divine donations and ghost taxes). Now that the local officials can all sympathize with the people's plight and are determined to reduce the burden on the people, they should thoroughly investigate in detail, and those that should be reduced should be reduced as much as possible (such as tobacco land and stamp tax), and those that should be prohibited should be strictly prohibited (such as miscellaneous fees and superstitions), so that the almost extinct lives of the people may have a glimmer of hope for recovery.

After returning the donation slips that I had read to the owner, I saw the woman holding a broom, sweeping the courtyard clean, first setting up five bowls and chopsticks and a plate of blue salt (there is a salt lake nearby, each liter weighs six or seven jin and sells for only one jiao of silver), and then taking out a large earthenware basin filled with thin porridge of millet, with a long-handled wooden spoon floating on top, and calling her children to drink on the ground (there was more soup than porridge, so it was called drinking). The woman had a niece who was already of marriageable age. She was also present at the time, with bright teeth and eyes, and was like a young lady from a modest family. Her sleeves were torn and her arms were completely exposed. At first glance, one would not suspect that she was a modern girl wearing a swimsuit and about to try bathing, but unfortunately, she was born in an economically bankrupt rural area and would never be able to see the backs of rich women in the city. Only at this moment did she lower her head and drink porridge, looking extremely embarrassed. It was inconvenient for the reporter to talk any further, so I bid farewell and returned to the inn, silently reciting the line "behind the vermilion gates, meat and wine go to waste, while on the road, there are those who freeze to death" incessantly. There were also wild barks coming from the rooftops. Looking up at the dog cages, many were placed on the roofs, which was also an innovation here.

Representatives of the Mongolian Political Committee Visit Chiang Kai-shek and Huang Fu to Petition

Beijing Dispatch: Bao Yueqing, a representative of the Mongolian Autonomous Political Committee, this morning (1st) carried the orders of Yun Yun, Chairman of the Committee, and De Wang, Secretary-General, to visit Chiang Kai-shek and Huang Fu respectively. The details are as follows:

Visiting Chiang Kai-shek

Bao Yueqing, the representative of the Mongolian Political Committee stationed in Peiping, previously received a telegram from Yun Wang and De Wang on the 26th, ordering him to welcome Chairman Chiang to Mongolia for guidance. At that time, Chiang was admitted to the hospital for a physical examination and it was inconvenient to visit him. Now that Chiang has been discharged from the hospital, he went to the headquarters at 9:10 a.m. today (1st) to meet him. Chiang received him in person. Bao first reported on the recent situation of the affairs of the Mongolian Political Committee and the situation in the Mongolian region. Then, he stated Yun and De Wang's sincere intention to welcome Chiang to Mongolia. Bao left at 10:00 a.m.

Visiting Huang Fu

After visiting Chiang Kai-shek, Bao, together with Bao Weihan, Meng He Batur, and Liang Zhixiang, representatives of the Mongolian Association in Peiping, went to the Political Consolidation Committee to visit Huang Fu at 10:30 a.m. He Qi Gong, the Secretary-General, received them on his behalf. Bao first stated the course of Han Fenglin's disappearance, and the sincere hope of the Mongolian Political Committee and the Mongolian Association in Peiping that the authorities would quickly find him. He also requested the Political Consolidation Committee to order the Peiping Municipal Authorities to be responsible for the search, and finally requested that the safety of the Mongolians residing in the interior be guaranteed in the future. He Qi Gong replied (1) Regarding the Han case, a submission was received from the Mongolian Association requesting assistance in the search. The Peiping Municipal Government has been ordered to transfer it to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. The results have not yet been reported and will be urged to expedite the matter. (2) The safety of the Mongolians can be absolutely guaranteed. (3) In the future, if there are any problems on the Mongolian side, representatives can be sent by the association, or written contact can be made with the Political Consolidation Committee, which will be responsible for handling them. Bao and others were very satisfied and left at around 11:00 a.m. (1st)

Rebuilding the Luan River Railway Bridge on the Peiping-Liaoning Railway

Materials Have Been Purchased from Britain

The Construction Period is Scheduled for Three Years

Tianjin Dispatch: The insurance period of the Luan River Great Iron Bridge on the Peiping-Liaoning Railway, 30 years, has long expired. The Railway Bureau has long planned to rebuild it, but due to the fact that North China has been plagued by events for many years, and that the section outside the pass has been forcibly cut off by the puppet state, the income is not as good as before. Therefore, it has been repeatedly stopped due to the lack of funds and the surrounding environment. This spring, the engineer of the Bureau inspected the bridge body and found that it was already leaning, and the bridge deck also had many cracks. Vehicles traveling to and fro had to change to a speed of no more than 15 miles per hour. However, it was still difficult to avoid danger, so the report was given to the Railway. After passing the Bureau Affairs Meeting, it was decided to save money from the Railway's surplus and raise 1 to 2 million Yuan over three years to rebuild it, widen the bridge deck, and change it to double tracks, so that traffic to and fro would not be delayed. The Bureau submitted it to the Ministry of Railways for approval and then started purchasing materials from various steel factories in Britain. It was originally planned to start construction next spring, but it was reported that the water level of the Luan River rose sharply this summer, and the bridge foundation was stirred up, becoming more and more tilted. In addition, the riverbed collapsed and the bridge body sank. It was even more dangerous for high-speed trains and freight trains to pass through. Therefore, the Bureau decided to advance the construction and telegraphed the British factory to expedite the delivery of materials. As of the 15th of this month, a part of the materials had been transported to Qinhuangdao and transferred to the side of the Luan River Railway Bridge for stacking. After the Engineering Office of the Railway Bureau sent personnel to inspect and accept them, it ordered engineers to lead hundreds of ironworkers and carpenters to take a special train to the east bank of Wanhe on the 26th of this month to build a temporary workshop and start work, building a new bridge next to the old bridge. Before the new bridge is completed, the old bridge will be repaired to avoid danger. The construction period is estimated to be three years, but if there is no problem with the funds, it can also be shortened to one and a half years.

It currently takes 18 hours and 50 minutes to travel to and from Guanwai. The Japanese side recently asked the Peiping-Liaoning Railway Bureau to open a special express train to shorten the travel time to 17 hours. The Railway Bureau has approved the Japanese side's request and plans to revise and implement it around November 15th. Only the time will be shortened compared to before, and the other methods will remain the same. The outside world previously rumored that a special express train would be added to the Peiping-Luan traffic, which was a misunderstanding of this matter. All trains on the Peiping-Liaoning Railway are also planned to shorten the time in the short term, so that each train can reach its destination faster. Although this has been planned recently, due to the fact that the roadbed has been in disrepair for a long time and that half of the sleepers are rotted, the materials and funds involved are quite large. Therefore, the Peiping-Tianjin section will be renovated first, and then the trunk line will be extended. (October 31st)

Jiangsu Finance Department Procures Grain for the Guiding the Huai River Project

The Agricultural Bank of China is Entrusted to Send Personnel to Shanghai to Purchase

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The project of guiding the Huai River into the sea started on the 1st, and the system of conscripted labor is completely adopted. There are 160,000 workers from 12 counties including Huaiyin. As for food, which is necessary for the workers' lives, about 2,000 dan of rice or 200,000 jin of flour are consumed every day. The Provincial Government has issued an order to the relevant counties, informing the merchants to supply them at flat prices as much as possible, and also entrusted the Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank to purchase crude wood and various kinds of third- and fourth-class flour, corn, and sorghum. According to Chief Xue, Director of General Affairs of the Provincial Farmers Bank, the Agricultural Bank is actively rushing to handle the purchase of rice and flour entrusted by the Provincial Government this time. Therefore, Vice-President Hou made a special trip to Shanghai a few days ago to contact the Agricultural Products Marketing Office of the Bank to discuss all the progress of purchasing rice flour and other items. Now Mr. Hou is in Shanghai, and it is likely that he has properly negotiated with the major flour mills in Shanghai. The number of purchases is not yet clear at this time, and it will be announced after Mr. Hou returns to Zhenjiang. He will return to the province no later than tomorrow (2nd). In order to actively handle the purchase of food, the Bank plans to send personnel to Wuhu in the next few days to contact the purchase of food. (2nd)

Tianjin Rongchang Match Factory Suspends Production

Tianjin Dispatch: The match industry in Tianjin has been flourishing since the beginning of the Republic of China. The manufacturers operated by Chinese businessmen include the Beiyang, Danhua, and Rongchang factories. The manufacturers operated by Japanese businessmen include the Daisheng and Sanyou factories. This spring, the Ministry of Finance increased the unified match tax. The three factories operated by Chinese businessmen have suffered losses and cannot bear the increased burden. They have jointly appealed to the match industry in Shandong Province to ask the Ministry of Finance to reduce or exempt the unified tax, but this has not been approved. At that time, the three factories in Tianjin once stopped production to express their firm attitude. Later, at the request of the workers, and with the mediation of the Party and government authorities, the entire factory resumed production and勉維艱局 (struggled to maintain the difficult situation). However, the business of each factory was affected by this blow, and it fell into a slump. Recently, due to the excessively high unified tax and high costs, especially under the special circumstances in Tianjin, Japanese merchants have tried to smuggle and sell a large number of counterfeit matches without paying taxes. Not only the sales outlets have been completely blocked, making it impossible to compete with Japanese merchants, but also the inventories have been piling up, making losses unbearable. On October 6th of this year, the Rongchang Fire Factory decided at a shareholders' meeting that due to slow sales and the combustibility of matches, the inventory in the warehouse had become extremely dangerous after a long time. The factory reported to the Party and government authorities to approve the official suspension of production in order to clear the inventory and reorganize the factory. However, the Party and government authorities believed that if the 2,500 workers of the factory were to lose their jobs once, not only would their lives be unsustainable, but also the order of Tianjin would be worrisome during this time of tight winter defense. Therefore, Ma Liang, a member of the Party Department, and Deng Qinglan, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, convened both labor and management of the factory to discuss ways to maintain operations and informed them of the pros and cons. After several consultations over the past ten days, the factory's attitude was resolute, and the suspension of production was inevitable, resulting in ineffective consultation. The Party and government authorities only supervised the factory to implement the conditional dismissal of workers. The method has been signed by representatives of both labor and management within this month. The dismissal procedures will be completed by the end of this month. The factory's property has been locked up by creditors and has begun to handle liquidation procedures. It is also heard that after Rongchang stops production, the other two factories operated by Chinese businessmen also have unstable news. The match industry in Tianjin is likely to go bankrupt from now on, and there will be no more domestically produced matches in North China. At the same time, at a time when the match industry in Tianjin is precarious, Japanese merchants are planning to invest in establishing a large-scale match factory, taking advantage of the opportunity of Rongchang's suspension of production to invest in dumping and infringing on the domestic market. If this matter is indeed realized, then the domestic match industry in North China will be completely bankrupt. (October 30th, Wang Shijun, our newspaper's correspondence student)

Songjiang

Falsely Claiming to be a Communist Party Member and Requesting Self-Renewal

The Executive Committee of the County previously received a local person, Lu Fengkang, who claimed to be a Communist Party member and requested self-renewal, confessing that he had committed robbery and other acts, and now he had repented, earnestly requesting to be allowed to renew himself. The committee followed the usual procedures, sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau, and at the same time instructed them to wait for verification and handling on file. It was reported that the committee recently found that Lu Fengkang was not a Communist Party member at all, and dared to falsely claim to be applying for self-renewal, obviously using the opportunity of self-renewal to try to evade responsibility for his crimes, which was extremely cunning. It was appropriate to send a letter to the County Government, requesting the County Court to order the arrest of the criminal for investigation and prosecution in order to warn against cunning.

Security Team Live Ammunition Shooting

In order to enhance the academic and technical skills of the students in the third district squad leader training class of the Provincial Security Team, live ammunition shooting will be held every Friday and Saturday from today (2nd) until the end of this month, a total of four times and eight days. It will be held at the Dajiao Field outside the South Gate and has been ordered to be followed.

New Education Director Takes Office

Zhu Zhaosheng, Director of the Education Bureau of this county, applied for resignation and was approved by the Education Department. After deliberation at the Provincial Government Conference, Shen Lianbi was appointed to succeed him. Mr. Shen is well-known in the education sector for his knowledge and experience. Now that he has been appointed, the education sector in Songyi will definitely be more colorful. Mr. Shen took office yesterday, and all the staff in the bureau remained in their positions in order to be familiar with the situation.

Kunshan

Autumn Harvest Assessment Rejected by the Province

Kunshan suffered a severe drought this year, with a total of 111,708 mu of farmland in the county yielding no harvest. However, the autumn assessment of the harvest was set at 8.785, which was rejected by the province after the county submitted it for review, and an order was issued to increase it slightly. At 2:00 p.m. on the 1st, the County Government convened a meeting of representatives from various agencies and district chiefs to discuss the results. It was decided that the district offices and public organizations would telegraph the province, listing the reasons why the autumn harvest could not be slightly increased, and that Cai Wu, Jie Lin, Gui Shen, Yan Huading, Zhu Wenyuan, and Dai Juong would be designated as representatives to go to the province on the 5th to fight for it.

Changshu

Meili Murder Case: Suspension of Request for Inspection

A few days ago, the Meili Public Security Bureau sent four policemen to Zhou Bingfu's house in West Street to arrest a sorcerer. However, due to the great momentum, Zhou's 16-year-old sick daughter, Zhou Yueqin, was frightened to death. At that time, the whole township was in an uproar, and the people blamed the Public Security Bureau. The Bureau immediately sent the responsible police officers, Ding Zheng and others, to the General Bureau for custody pending investigation. The family of the deceased was suing the County Government, but Director Zhou handed the responsible four policemen over to the judiciary for review, posted bail, and sent them back to the original bureau to temporarily maintain their duties. Now, because the woman's abdomen was only enlarged after being frightened to death, and there were no other special signs, the family of the deceased suspended the request for inspection by the county and filed a complaint for negligent homicide. The body was already buried by the family on the afternoon of the 30th. It is said that a private settlement has been reached.

Suzhou

Wang Shaoyou Comes to Suzhou to Investigate Land

Wang Shaoyou, investigator of the Jiangsu Special Zone Land Committee, concurrently commissioner of the Provincial Party Headquarters, and party affairs investigator, has been conducting a comprehensive survey of land in Suzhou. He has inspected places such as Paiguan, Lishi, Guoxiang, and Lumu. Now, Wang has received a telegram from the Provincial Party Headquarters, ordering him to investigate the work of the county party headquarters, district party headquarters, and sub-district party branches in the special zone, and he will set off for the investigation soon.

Four Garrison Zones Divided During Winter Defense Period

Magistrate Wu believes that this county is adjacent to Taihu Lake and has a flourishing commercial market. For this year's winter defense, he has specially divided the area into four garrison zones as follows: (1) Inside and outside the city; (2) Part of the City Temple, and Bendu, Guangfu, Panguan, Hengjing, Dongshan, and Xishan; (3) Huangdai, Xiangcheng, and Weiting; (4) Chefang, Xietang, Zaizhi, and Zhouzhuang. The county magistrate will serve as the overall commander, and the police and security teams from each township will be responsible for garrisoning. When necessary, they may request assistance from local troops.

Su-Mu and Su-Chang Roads to Open to Traffic Next Spring

The Su-Mu Road from Suzhou City to Mudu is now under construction, and the roadbed of the Su-Chang Road from Suzhou to Changshu has also been fully completed. Both roads are expected to be open to traffic in February next year. However, the Su-Chang Road is a branch of the Xi-Hu Road, and in the future, long-distance buses on this road will be operated by the Xi-Hu Company.

Telegraph and Telephone Bureaus Merged

The Suzhou Telegraph Bureau and the Telephone Bureau have been merged to form the Wu County Telegraph Bureau. Niu Yinchu, the original director of the Telephone Bureau, has been reappointed as the director, and he will also be in charge of the Wujiang and Pingwang Bureaus, as well as adding postal collection and delivery points. Director Niu is also working on telephone services in various townships, and telephone service to Huxuguan will be available by the end of this year.

District Chiefs Resolutely Resign

The autonomous region of Wu County was originally divided into 23 districts, but it has now been reorganized into 13 districts. As a result, the area of each district has been expanded, and the operating funds for the shipping industry have been reduced by two-thirds. Furthermore, they have been ordered to handle the baojia system. The district chiefs feel that it is difficult to handle affairs, so Wu Erchang, district chief of the first district, Wang Deshou, district chief of the second district, Zhu Shanqing, district chief of the sixth district, and Zhang Hong, district chief of the ninth district, have all submitted their resignations. Although County Magistrate Wu has earnestly tried to persuade them to stay, the district chiefs have continued to submit their resignations due to lack of funds, and have resolutely resigned.

Haimen

It is Not Easy to Eradicate the Pirates of Lvsi

Recently, six pirate ships suddenly appeared off the coast of Lvsi, with more than 100 pirates. They robbed fishermen, kidnapped people for ransom, and committed all kinds of evils. The entire 13th Brigade of the Water Police set off the day before yesterday to encircle and suppress them. Peng Xiaochao, chief of staff of the Nantong District Command, was also invited to Lvsi to direct the operation. Yesterday (the 31st) afternoon, he came from Lvsi to Haimen and met with County Magistrate Chen, giving detailed instructions on the county's coastal defense. According to Peng, the pirates of Lvsi have been somewhat suppressed after being attacked by the police and militia, but they are constantly moving around, making it difficult to eradicate them completely in the short term. Peng then returned to Nantong by the same vehicle.

Shen Chujiang's Son Released After Being Kidnapped

Wu Bao, the 11-year-old son of Shen Chujiang, a wealthy household in Liuzhou Township, Fourth District, was kidnapped by bandits on the 24th day of the first month of the lunar calendar this year and a ransom of 10,000 yuan was demanded. After Shen reported the case to the county government, the police were ordered to arrest the suspects Lu Zaming and Jin Zigao. After repeated interrogations, there was no clue. The day before yesterday (the 28th), Wu Bao suddenly returned home. According to him, he was moved several times after being kidnapped and was now released. A bandit escorted him to the east of Sanyang Town in the Fourth District and left. The bandit had a letter for Wu Bao to bring back, stating that they should immediately compensate for the loss of 600 yuan, otherwise they would be in serious trouble later. Yesterday (the 31st), Shen presented the letter to the county government for investigation.

The Ministry of Communications, in order to save public funds and improve efficiency, has planned to merge the postal and telegraph bureaus. This matter has been rumored for a long time but has not been implemented. Now, the telegraph bureau in this county is merging. This matter has been rumored for a long time but has not been implemented. Now, the telegraph bureau in this county is installing wiring and equipment in the post office, and various projects are being completed one after another. Yesterday (the 2nd), the telegraph department was moved into the post office first. Land Survey in the Third District Completed

The Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau Survey Team has been surveying land in the Third District of the county for several months. All the plains have been surveyed. Recently, the survey team moved to Baohua Nunnery, west of Baojie Changqiao, to survey the mountainous fields in Qingqi Township. The work of surveying mountainous fields is more difficult than surveying flat fields. Yesterday, the district was completely surveyed. The team leader Huang Hui, the captain Zhou Houxi, and the land surveyor Tang Baoqi drew up maps and presented them to the provincial bureau, and then transferred to Gaochun for surveying. This is because the other districts of Xiyi will use aerial surveying.

County Government Schedules Winter Defense

The county government of this county, in view of the recent unrest among the old bandits and the frequent occurrence of theft cases, in order to consolidate defense and maintain peace and tranquility, has advanced the winter defense, established a winter defense headquarters in the Security Brigade, and divided the autonomous regions of the county into five joint defense zones based on local conditions. A joint defense office will be set up in the important district offices in each joint defense zone. The garrison security team or local police in each joint defense zone, as well as the lookout posts, should be under the command of the joint defense director during the winter defense period. The joint defense date will begin on the 15th of this month, and it is stipulated that there will be two joint sentry duties each month. If a bandit alarm occurs in a neighboring area, a team should be dispatched to pursue and capture the bandits, regardless of territorial boundaries.

The entire line is scheduled to be completed and open to traffic by October of the 24th year.

Local News

Anti-Disaster Drill to Be Held in This City from Midnight Tonight to Dawn

All Party, Government, and Military Organizations to Participate

Sirens to Be Used as Signals, More Than 20,000 People Mobilized

City Divided into Five Districts for Separate Drills

To Cultivate Citizens' Knowledge of Disaster Prevention

The Shanghai Municipal Government and the Songhu Garrison Command, considering that Shanghai is adjacent to the coast and that typhoons and high tides often occur in the autumn and summer every year, although no accidents have occurred, local people are always worried when alarms are issued. In order to cultivate the disaster prevention knowledge of local military police and mass organizations, a large-scale disaster relief drill will be held from 12:30 tonight until dawn. The following is a report from a New News Agency reporter who has learned about the situation:

Drill Intended to Simulate Disaster

The important purpose of this large-scale drill is to enable the staff of military and police agencies and mass organizations in this city to understand the knowledge of emergency handling in the event of a major disaster and to cultivate a connected protective ability so that they can respond appropriately when necessary. The object of today's drill is to assume that Shanghai will suddenly experience extremely violent storms and heavy rain from 12:30 on the night of November 3 until dawn. At the same time, electric lights, telephones, telegraph poles, and a portion of the houses in Huazhaibei, Nanshi, and Pudong have been damaged, causing fierce fires. Some unscrupulous elements took advantage of the fire to rob and cause disturbances, and the whole city was plunged into extreme chaos and terror. At this very critical moment, the military police and the public of the city should adopt protective measures.

All Sectors of the City to Participate

The organizations and groups participating in this drill include: the Municipal Government, the Songhu Garrison Command, the 5th Regiment of Military Police, the Municipal Security Office, the Municipal Public Security Bureau, the Municipal Defense Committee, the Municipal National Military Training Association, the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, the Public Works Bureau, the Health Bureau, the Social Affairs Bureau, the Education Bureau, the Ministry of Communications, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, the Ministry of Military Affairs, the Radio Station, the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Boy Scouts Council, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the General Trade Union, the Chinese Red Cross Society, the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, the China Electric Company, the China Aviation Company, the Hongqiao Airport, the Cover Team, the Inland Water Company, the China Motor Company, the Hu Min Long-Distance Bus Company, the Hu Tai Long-Distance Bus Company, the Public Utilities Bureau Bus Management Office, and other 29 agencies and groups.

Five Districts Divided for Easy Command

Assuming that after the disaster occurred, the commander of the Songhu Garrison immediately declared martial law in order to maintain order and rescue from the disaster and issued a mobilization order, dividing the city into five districts and appointing Yang Hu, director of the Security Office, and Wen Hongen, director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, as the chief commanders. The following is a record of the district troops, agencies, groups, and commanders: (1) Hunan District, including the jurisdiction of the Ximen and Shiliupu Branches of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. The commander is Wen Hongen, director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Guan Gong, director of the Shiliupu Branch, Zhu Haishan, captain of the Water Patrol Team, and Lu Ying, captain of the Detective Team, will command separately; (2) Hubei District, including the jurisdiction of the Xinzha and Zhan Branches of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. The commander is Chen Danmin, commander of the First Regiment of the Security Patrol Team; (3) Huxi District, including the jurisdiction of the Caojiadu Branch of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau (except for the Caohejing Police Station). The commander is Qi Xueqi, commander of the Second Regiment of the Security Team; (4) Pudong District, including the jurisdiction of the Pudong and Gaoqiao Branches of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. The commander is Zhang Mingqin, director of the Pudong Sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau; (5) Downtown District, including the jurisdiction of the Downtown Branch of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. The commander is Huang Qiguang, director of the branch; (6) The General Reserve Team, with the 5th Regiment of Military Police as the general reserve team, located near Longhua. (The Caohejing Police Station of the Public Security Bureau is responsible for guarding the vicinity of the駐地 and the Longhua Airport. The Caojing Police Station and the Caojing District Defense Corps are on guard in their respective locations, under the command of Lan Yundong of the Military Police Regiment; (7) The Investigation Team of the Garrison Command (except for mobilized soldiers) is concentrated in the Command to perform investigation, communication, and liaison tasks. It is estimated that more than 20,000 people will be mobilized.

Regulations on Drill Matters in Each District

The drill matters are divided into (A) Alert: when each district designates a factory to sound a siren for three minutes, the military and police agencies and teams will gather and then drill (A) suppressing riots and (B) arresting wanted criminals; (B) Disaster Relief: fire brigades, Red Cross societies, student teams, boy scouts, and other groups will gather and then drill (A) rushing to rescue (by the Shiliupu Branch and Dongjiadu Police Station in Hunan District), (B) fighting fires (by Hubei District), (C) repairing traffic (by Huxi District), and (D) rescuing the wounded (by Hubei District); (C) Public Training: the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Education Bureau, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau will send personnel to publicize and guide the public to understand emergency handling measures in the event of a disaster (hypothetical).

Post Notices to Inform the Public

The Shanghai Municipal Government and the Songhu Garrison Command, in addition to verbally notifying the Public Concession Police Department, the French Concession Police Department, the Japanese Marine Corps Command in Shanghai, and the British Garrison Command in Shanghai, jointly issued a notice stating: "Shanghai is an important place for industry and commerce with a dense population. The Songhu area is located on the coast, and there is a risk of typhoons from the sea in summer and autumn. In order to prevent the worst and to awaken the public's attention to disaster prevention, the mayor will gather all relevant agencies and mass organizations to conduct a disaster relief drill on the night of November 3, from 12:30 to dawn. However, this is a pioneering event, and we are afraid that the public will not understand the truth, leading to misunderstandings. In addition to reporting and ordering separately, we hereby issue a notice to inform the public." This notice is dated November 2, 23rd year of the Republic of China, Mayor and Commander Wu Tiecheng.

Pilots of Songhan District Petition Party and Government Yesterday

Requesting a Stop to the Arbitrary Actions of the Pilotage Management Committee

Shipping Association Sends Letter to Minister Kong Stating Opinions

After the new rules of the China Pilotage Management Committee, Songhan District, were announced and implemented, the shipping companies decided to suspend shipping and telegraphed for appeals. The Songhan Pilotage Joint Petition Group petitioned the party and government agencies yesterday, and the Shipping Association sent a letter to Minister Kong stating the process. The details are as follows:

Pilotage Petition

According to the National News Agency, the Songhan Pilotage Joint Petition Group, due to the unresolved pilotage dispute, sent more than ten representatives, including Li Yushan, to the Municipal Government at 10:00 a.m. yesterday to petition Mayor Wu. Secretary Chen received them on behalf of the mayor. In addition to submitting a written petition, the group also made four points in person: (1) When China is recovering its navigation rights, pilotage is particularly important. Please pay attention to national sovereignty and do not allow customs officials to arbitrarily control it; (2) Our pilot colleagues have all served in the shipping industry for many years and have considerable experience and licenses, which cannot be compared with newcomers; (3) There are many dark secrets in the pilotage examination. The qualified personnel recruited are mostly selected based on personal bias and lack the ability to serve. The refusal of employment by various industry professionals can prove this; (4) Please, Mayor, prioritize national sovereignty and rescue our colleagues. Secretary Chen replied that the mayor expressed deep sympathy for the points in the petition and would immediately prepare a document to submit to the Central Government and consult the Ministry of Finance, the Navy, and the Ministry of Communications, etc. Afterwards, they went to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to petition Director Wu. Wu was busy with official business and instructed Secretary Hu to receive them on his behalf, stating that all points in the petition could be remedied. Afterwards, they transferred to the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters at Fenglin Bridge, where Tian Zhou Dize received them and believed that the point raised by the group regarding the many dark secrets in the customs examination needed to be studied and planned to send personnel to the customs to investigate the truth of the examination in the coming days. Later, the group went to the Seamen's Special Party Headquarters, where Qian Zhaochang received them and believed that the seamen's profession was being devastated by foreigners without any guarantee, and decided to submit the matter to the Central Government for instructions.

Shipping Industry's Opinion

According to the New News Agency, Qing Hede, chairman of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, sent a letter to Minister of Finance Kong yesterday, stating: "Minister Yongzhi, I respectfully inform you that I recently read in the newspaper that you met with reporters and gave a speech, stating that shipping companies should not oppose the pilotage examination. I am deeply grateful for your concern for the shipping industry. However, the content of your speech seems to have some discrepancies with the actual situation of the shipping companies' appeal. I am afraid that it will cause misunderstandings. I would like to state this to you. The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association believes that the new Shanghai Pilotage Management Committee has greatly increased the pilotage rates for Chinese pilots in Songhan, which is unbearable. Therefore, after a collective discussion, it was decided to appeal to the Yuan and the Ministry to request a reduction. In recent years, the shipping industry has declined to the extreme. The Chinese shipping industry has already imposed a 30% tonnage tax to fund the merchant shipping school, and it has also increased its burden due to the establishment of the Shipping Administration Bureau. It is already struggling to maintain its current state. If the burden is further increased, it will be impossible. Since it concerns our own interests, we cannot remain silent. I hope you will understand our plight. As for the committee's screening of the national short-term pilots who have received licenses from the Ministry of the Navy, the shipping companies have not expressed any opposition. As you said, it is extremely important in relation to life and property. Life is valued by everyone, and ships are the only property of shipping companies. How can we not take care of them? Although we are foolish, we should also understand this. However, the examination conducted by the pilotage association this time is only for Chinese people and not for foreigners. Since there is no issue of sovereignty, and pilotage is different from driving, the most important thing is familiarity with the sea routes. Chinese pilots in Songhan mostly come from experience and have very few academics. Therefore, we also contribute our opinions that, during the examination, except for those who fail on their own or have diseases, service experience should be the prerequisite to maintain livelihoods. There is no fact of opposing the examination or screening. The documents are available for review. I also ask you to appreciate the original facts and give your support so that the truth can be revealed and the issue can be resolved. I sincerely pray for your success and wish you all the best."

Plain Text Telegrams Will Not Be Translated Separately

The Ministry of Communications previously issued an order to telegram offices across the country stating that, starting from November 1st, all Chinese plain text telegrams should be translated and sent uniformly. However, the Shanghai Telegraph Office, considering the psychology of the Shanghai business community, who are unwilling for telegrams to be translated to avoid leaking secrets and to prevent delays, has decided that, in order to respect the wishes of the recipients, starting from the day before yesterday, unless the recipient sends a letter requesting translation, all other telegrams will still be delivered in code and will not be translated separately.

Page 10

The General Association of Drivers Petitions the Ministry of Communications to Protest the Hong Kong Government's Examination of Chinese Ship Masters

China Has Joined the International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea

Certificates Issued by the Government Should Receive Equal Treatment

The new ships Hai Yuan, etc., of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, due to the Hong Kong authorities' insistence on examining Chinese ship masters, have resulted in the Hai Yuan employing foreign crew members. The Shanghai Commercial Ship Driving Association strongly disagrees with this and lodged a protest yesterday, which has been submitted to the Ministry of Communications, stating that for passenger ships sailing to Hong Kong, Chinese captains should not be subject to examination by the Hong Kong government in order to maintain international equality and uphold sovereignty. According to reports, the Si Hai ships ordered by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company in England are about to be completed one after another, and the Hai Yuan has already arrived in Shanghai. The company plans to have the Hai Yuan operate on the Shanghai-Hong Kong-Guangdong line and, it is said, intends to appoint foreigners as captains because the Hong Kong government requires Chinese captains to pass their examinations before being allowed to serve. China has already joined the International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea and should stand on an equal footing internationally. The captain's certificates issued by the Chinese government, having been recognized by the Chinese government as qualified to ensure safety at sea, should have the same effect as captain's certificates issued by other countries. If foreign commercial ships sailing to China have captain's certificates issued by their governments, China also recognizes them as qualified, and Chinese captains on commercial ships sailing abroad should receive equal treatment. This is a self-evident international reciprocal relationship. If the Hong Kong government recognizes the captain's certificates of other countries as valid but refuses to recognize the captain's certificates issued by the Chinese government, insisting on examination, it not only despises the Chinese nation but also has no basis in any convention. Could there be any greater inequality in treatment? If the governments of other countries follow this example and also examine Chinese captains on commercial ships sailing to various countries, the consequences for China's international shipping industry would be unimaginable, and the country's international standing would fall to an unknown degree. What national sovereignty would there be to speak of? The reason why Chinese captains should not be subject to examination by the Hong Kong government is not out of fear of difficulty or an attempt to avoid it but, from the standpoint of sovereignty, there is simply no need to be subjected to their examination. Furthermore, Chinese captains have been serving on commercial ships sailing to Hong Kong for many years, with ships such as the Shun Feng, Gong Ping, and Kun Xing all having achieved considerable success, demonstrating that the qualifications of Chinese captains are not inferior to those of other countries. Therefore, the Hong Kong government has no excuse not to recognize the certificates issued by the Chinese government. It is earnestly requested that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs be consulted to make a reasoned argument and lodge a protest to maintain international equality and uphold sovereignty, which would be fortunate for the country. (Remainder omitted.) This petition was sent out yesterday.

The Banking Law Research Association Has Achieved Considerable Results

Opinions Submitted by Banks in Shanghai and Other Cities

Ten Articles Are Planned to Be Submitted for Amendment

According to the Central News Agency, the Banking Law Research Committee organized by the Shanghai Banking Association has held several meetings to discuss and study the Banking Law. The Central News Agency reporter inquired about this with the committee yesterday morning. It was learned that the Banking Law regulations were promulgated in 1931, totaling fifty-two articles, but have not been implemented since their promulgation. At a time when the banking industry is extremely developed and social finance is extremely fearful, the Ministry of Finance authorities and leaders of the banking industry across the country deeply feel that the implementation of the Banking Law is urgent and cannot be delayed any longer. Banking colleagues believe that the previously promulgated Banking Law has shortcomings, and the Ministry of Finance authorities also fear that if the previously promulgated Banking Law is implemented suddenly, requests for amendments will inevitably arise. Therefore, they have exchanged views with the banking industry in advance and will amend and implement it to make it more complete. Thus, the Banking Law Research Committee was organized. The committee has held several meetings and has achieved considerable results. It still needs one or two more meetings before it can conclude its research, which is expected to be completed within this week. In order to gather the opinions of the banking industry across the country, the committee has notified banks in Shanghai and other cities separately to compile opinion letters and send them to the committee for research, and has set a deadline for banks in Shanghai to submit them within five days. Now that the deadline has passed, many opinion letters from various banks have been received. Due to the greater distances involved, not all submissions from other cities have been received yet. It is expected that responses from banks in Beiping, Tianjin, and other cities will arrive within days. After the committee receives all the opinion letters, it will compile and study them, and then submit them to the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Banking Association. The Executive Committee will then convene a full meeting to discuss them in detail, and submit the results of the discussion to the Ministry of Finance for transmission to the Legislative Yuan for amendment and implementation of the previously promulgated Banking Law. The opinions of various bankers on amending the previously promulgated Banking Law have not yet reached the time for publication, but it is understood that ten articles of the previously promulgated fifty-two articles of the Banking Law are planned to be submitted for amendment.

The Banking Society Invited Yu Huan Cheng to Speak on the Silver Tax Problem

Raise the Export Point of Silver and Suppress Outflow

The Fundamental Solution Lies in Controlling International Trade

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the Banking Society invited Yu Huan Cheng, former Deputy Governor of the Bank of China, to speak on the "Minor Silver Tax Problem" at the Shanghai Banking Association's meeting hall on Hong Kong Road at 7 PM last night. Over a hundred bank members attended the lecture. Yu's main points were as follows: "Regarding the minor silver tax, I made this proposal four years ago in a speech at the Central News Agency. At that time, silver prices were falling sharply, and there were many silver imports, so I advocated a small import tax to maintain the equalization of our country's foreign exchange. Now that silver prices have risen, changing imports into exports, a small export tax is added. Although the matter is the opposite, the reason for equalizing foreign exchange rates is the same. The effect of adding a silver export tax is firstly to raise the export point of silver, which is sufficient to suppress the outflow of silver; secondly, to invisibly increase tariffs, making foreign exchange for imported goods firm and increasing their prices; and thirdly, to balance foreign exchange. Although foreign exchange has risen sharply after the increase, this is a temporary phenomenon. However, in our opinion, those who seek perfection in balancing foreign exchange should have an ideal standard for balancing foreign exchange. When prices rise and fall, the market should be balanced by buying and selling by the Equalization Committee, so that those engaged in international trade do not take great risks. Secondly, the equalization fund still needs to be increased, and various banks engaged in foreign exchange should be united to strengthen their strength. However, these are all stopgap measures. The fundamental solution is to eliminate the huge trade deficit in international trade, so that cash will not flow out. There are proposals to control exchange rates to save the trade deficit, and there are proposals to control trade. In China's current situation, seeking to control exchange rates is no less difficult than controlling trade, so I advocate the latter. However, there must be full preparation, and it is hoped that those with aspirations will engage in research."
