Shanghai Municipal Council Considers Japanese Residents' Proposal to Reform Education Policy

A Japanese residents' organization in this city has suggested to the Municipal Council to change its education policy. The main points are: (1) Abolish municipal schools; (2) Subsidize schools run by various expatriate organizations; (3) The total annual subsidy should be based on the total amount of recurrent and temporary education expenses for this year; (4) The allocation standard should be determined based on the number of students or the amount of taxes paid. This proposal was submitted to the Education Committee for discussion, and Japanese representatives Mr. Sugimoto and Mr. Ikeda were invited to the meeting to present their views.

According to a report submitted by the acting head of the Finance Department, in 1933, there were 6,591 expatriate students in municipal and municipal-funded schools, about half of whom were Japanese. If half of this year's recurrent and temporary expenses for foreign schools were used to subsidize Japanese schools according to the proposal, the deficit would exceed 700,000 yuan. However, the actual subsidy is only 118,000 yuan. The amount of self-funding by the Japanese side is about 327,000 yuan. Tuition is clearly minimal, with a maximum of only five yuan per month. Later, Mr. Ikeda stated that the Japanese residents' proposal was intended to seek a fair distribution of funds, but complete adoption seemed to be very difficult. Therefore, reasonable revisions would not be opposed. However, the current system of the Municipal Council would require more donations to expand further. In any case, the increase in funding would not allow all students within the boundary to receive education. Therefore, how can the increase in funding be continued without reaching a limit? Why not allocate more of the funds so that students outside the municipal schools can benefit? The current establishment of municipal schools is quite beneficial to wealthy families, while nine-tenths of the others are unable to attend due to high tuition fees. As for changing the policy, it can be done gradually. First, the current construction costs could be transferred to subsidies.

One committee member said that there are several standards for the distribution of funds. In terms of population, there are 18,478 Japanese (5,438 under the age of 15) and 17,993 other foreigners (3,493 under the age of 15) within and outside the boundaries. There are 971,397 Chinese (253,388 under the age of 15). In terms of the amount of taxes paid, the Japanese account for 7.5%, other foreigners 50.4%, and Chinese 42.1%. Which standard should be adopted must be investigated.

Mr. Ikeda replied that whether the distribution should be strictly and equally determined according to residents and nationality could be considered by the Municipal Council. However, the current budget for education expenses seems to have reached its highest level. Even if the Municipal Council's revenue increases, it can only subsidize private schools with its surplus. In terms of student treatment, each Japanese student costs about 60 or 70 yuan per year, while other foreign students cost up to 400 yuan per student per year, which is a big difference.

The chairman of the committee stated that the tuition fees paid by students in municipal schools are based on one-third of the total expenses of the school. Mr. Ikeda said that the Japanese schools have different methods. In addition to subsidies from the Japanese government and the Municipal Council, everything is borne by Japanese organizations. As for the tuition fees, they are investigated based on the ability of the parents and assigned accordingly. It is now estimated that the expenditure for 1935 will be 587,000 yuan, while the income is only 539,000 yuan.

After further discussion, it was clarified that the Municipal Council's responsibility is only to plan education for the children of residents or taxpayers within the boundary. If there are students from the French Concession or the Chinese area in municipal schools, one-quarter of the tuition fee will be added. However, it is not easy to restrict subsidies, as subsidized schools will inevitably admit children from outside the boundary or who are not taxpayers.

One committee member said that the Municipal Council's education expenses have doubled in the past three years and now account for 89% of the total revenue. However, another committee member said that the education plan adopted four years ago was the minimum and not the maximum. The need to increase the number of schools now is as urgent as it was in the past. Although the plan has been slightly halted, the public hopes that it will resume next year. At this point, the committee announced that the meeting was adjourned.

Page 16

Autumn Special Issue

The Reclusive Scholar, the Chrysanthemum

— Only Through

To be a follower, clinging to the powerful, rushing towards all the excitement—everyone says that this is not the type of person you want to be. Therefore, in the seasons of spring and summer, when all the flowers are blooming and fawning, it is difficult to find famous flowers with noble character. Even if there are any, they are mixed in with all the purples and reds, and in the eyes of the general flower appreciator, they just seem like one of the three thousand hangers-on. Therefore, in the autumn wind, when all the purples and reds have faded and lost their luster, the chrysanthemum, which blooms, is called a "reclusive scholar".

The reason why the chrysanthemum is called a "reclusive scholar" is not only because it doesn't cling to the powerful, it isn't running to fawn on others, it doesn't squeeze into the three thousand hangers-on, and it doesn't blossom and fade with the masses. Even in terms of appearance, it has unique characteristics. The stems and leaves of ordinary flowers all have a common characteristic, which is that they are very plump. If there is not enough fertilizer to make them plump, then they cannot release beautiful flowers. The chrysanthemum is not like this. Even without fertilizer, it can bloom. With fertilizer, there are still only a few sparse stems. Moreover, potted plants are not as elegant as those that grow by the eastern fence. This is the nature of "accustomed to being a mountain man, free and easy".

Ordinary flowers, except for woody plants, rely on deeply rooted trunks and branches, and can still sprout and bloom next spring. The rest, after the autumn wind sweeps through, after the summer heat recedes, all wither into dead grass. The chrysanthemum is not like this. Although the chrysanthemum is an herbaceous plant, after it has bloomed, it still survives, waiting for next autumn to sprout and bloom again, with clear, noble, elegant, and light flowers, to embellish this extremely bleak autumn scene. Moreover, although chrysanthemums bloom, they do not leave seeds, but are propagated by division of branches, unlike ordinary flowers, which strive for expansion of power. One flower can contain dozens or even hundreds of seeds.

However, in this era of rampant human desires, the reclusive scholar, who does not fawn, does not cling to power, is content with indifference, and does not compete with the world, is no longer valued. Because today's so-called reclusive scholars are, in name, living in the mountains, cultivating their nature, watching waterfalls, and listening to autumn winds. In reality, they are unable to forget the pleasures of music, women, horses, and dogs. They are merely temporarily frustrated, and they call themselves reclusive scholars, waiting for the opportunity to come. Or, because their wallets are overflowing with official wealth, they retire to the mountains and forests, with a charming wife on the left and a beautiful concubine on the right, just to change the air. The chrysanthemum is called a reclusive scholar, and these people are also called reclusive scholars. I think the chrysanthemum cannot bear this mass of wealth and luxury.

Key Points of the Republic of China Criminal Code Amendment Passed by the Legislative Yuan

I. The chapter count and titles in the General Provisions section of the current law that have been added, deleted, revised, or merged in this bill are as follows:

(I) In the Chapter on Legal Examples, all articles related to relatives have been deleted because provisions already exist in the Family Law of the Civil Code. The remaining articles are few, so this bill merges them into one article attached to the Chapter on Legal Precedents, thus deleting the former chapter.

(II) Within the Chapter on Temporal Examples, provisions already exist in the Civil Code, such as those regarding the calculation of time periods. Others are already covered in prison regulations, such as the timeframes for releasing prisoners on parole. These have been deleted, leaving only one article concerning the calculation of criminal sentences. This bill merges that article into the Chapter on Penalties, thus deleting the former chapter.

(III) Most articles in the Chapter on Criminal Responsibility and Mitigation of Penalties concern issues of criminal responsibility. Only the article on self-reporting specifically concerns penalty mitigation. Therefore, this bill moves that article into the Chapter on the Discretionary Imposition and Aggravation/Mitigation of Penalties, and the chapter title is simplified to Criminal Responsibility.

(IV) "Attempt" refers to an incomplete crime; there is no so-called "attempted crime." Therefore, this bill changes the Chapter on Attempted Crimes to Chapter on Attempted Offenses.

(V) The articles in the Chapter on Penalties cover not only types of penalties but also their severity, execution, pronouncement, and credit for detention. Therefore, this bill shortens the title to "Penalties."

(VI) Most articles in the current law's Chapter on Combined Offenses concern issues of multiple offenses being punished together. Therefore, this bill changes the title to Multiple Offenses Punished Together.

(VII) This bill merges the Chapter on Discretionary Penalties and the Chapter on Examples of Aggravation/Mitigation into one chapter to simplify matters.

(VIII) Recent criminal policy emphasizes social defense. Newly revised criminal codes in various countries include detailed provisions on security measures. While the current law includes provisions for juvenile offenders and mentally ill individuals, such as moral reformation, education, behavior supervision, and imprisonment, the scope is too narrow. This bill specifically adds a Chapter on Security Measures.

II. The current law's Article 2 does not have provisions for intermediary laws and uses only the severity of old and new laws as the standard for comparison, which seems inadequate. Therefore, this bill adds provisions for intermediary laws. Except for custodial measures, which should absolutely follow the new law, if the law before the judgment is more favorable to the perpetrator, then the provisions most favorable to the perpetrator in the law at the time of the act or in the intermediary law should be used for the verdict. Furthermore, if the law changes after the verdict has been finalized and no longer punishes the act, there seems to be no need to continue executing the sentence. Therefore, this bill adds this provision as well.

III. Criminal acts committed on Chinese aircraft flying outside of the country's territory should also be subject to Chinese criminal law. Therefore, this bill adds this provision.

IV. Enslaving people is an internationally prohibited act. Furthermore, public officials who commit embezzlement in a foreign country while on duty should also be punished according to Chinese criminal law. Therefore, this bill adds these provisions separately.

V. According to the current law's Article 7, the Republic of China Criminal Code applies too broadly to citizens of the Republic of China and to people outside of the territory of the Republic of China or foreign citizens who commit crimes against citizens of the Republic of China outside of the territory of the Republic of China, for which the minimum sentence is imprisonment. This bill revises this to only apply to crimes for which the minimum sentence is imprisonment of three years or more.

VI. The current law does not have explicit provisions regarding the causal relationship between passive acts and criminal facts, which causes difficulties in application. Therefore, this bill adds these provisions.

VII. The current law refers to all aggravations or mitigations of penalties as "original sentence." In reality, when there is progressive aggravation or mitigation, or when aggravation and mitigation occur in succession, what is being aggravated or mitigated is the aggravated or mitigated sentence, not the original sentence. Therefore, this bill changes the wording to "the sentence."

VIII. According to current law, ignorance of the law can only result in a reduction of the sentence based on the circumstances, which seems too harsh. This bill changes "ignorance of the law" to "ignorance of the law" and allows for exemption from punishment under certain conditions.

IX. The focus should be on moral reformation and education for juvenile offenders. Therefore, this bill raises the age of responsibility to fourteen and the age for reduced punishment to eighteen. At the same time, it specifies the provisions for moral reformation, education, behavior supervision, and other measures in detail within the Chapter on Security Measures to provide for redress.

X. The current law adopts a mandatory reduction of punishment for people with mental deficiencies and those who are deaf or mute, which seems too lenient. This bill changes it to an option for reduction.

XI. Committing a crime while intoxicated is naturally punishable by law, and there is no need for special provisions. Therefore, this bill deletes Article 32 of the current law.

XII. The current law punishes lower-level public officials for official actions taken under the orders of their superiors, regardless of whether they knew the orders were illegal, which seems too harsh. Therefore, this bill adds an exception clause.

XIII. The current law adopts a discretionary reduction or exemption for impossible attempts and limits it to cases where the methods of the crime could never produce the intended result. This bill changes it to where reduction or exemption must be granted for cases where there is no danger, regardless of whether the method or the objective is impossible, which seems more appropriate.

XIV. Instigating a crime is a particularly malicious act that should be punished independently. However, punishing the instigator with the full sentence of the completed crime when the instigated person did not commit the crime or committed it but failed seems excessive. Therefore, this bill stipulates that such situations should be treated as attempted crimes.

XV. This bill stipulates that accomplices are always eligible for a reduced sentence, allowing judges to exercise discretion based on the circumstances to achieve fairness.

XVI. The current law does not specify the maximum period for aggravated detention, which seems inadequate. This bill stipulates a limit of four months to differentiate it from imprisonment.

XVII. The standards for the severity of principal penalties have issues that cannot be resolved by Article 51 of the current law, such as issues of exclusive penalties, elective penalties, and concurrent penalties. Therefore, this bill makes appropriate revisions.

XVIII. This bill changes the provisions of the current law regarding deprivation of public rights to only include the loss of qualifications as a public official. The loss of other qualifications should be specified in various related laws for greater convenience. Furthermore, this bill clearly specifies the conditions for declaring or being able to declare the loss of qualifications as a public official in the General Provisions, and it deletes all articles related to the deprivation of public rights in the Special Provisions to achieve simplicity.

XIX. The Temporary New Criminal Law's provisions regarding the conversion of short-term imprisonment to fines were not adopted by the current law. As a result, people sentenced to short-term imprisonment must be sent to prison regardless of any impediments, which is quite inconvenient in practice. Moreover, it is difficult to avoid those who commit crimes accidentally acquiring bad habits due to short-term imprisonment. Many in the legal community have advocated for restoring this system. Therefore, this bill allows the conversion to fines under strict conditions.

XX. The current law sets the payment period for fines at one month, which seems too short. This bill changes it to two months. The current law allows for imprisonment in lieu of fines for up to one year, which can be confused with short-term imprisonment. This bill changes it to only allowing labor in lieu of fines and sets the limit at six months. Furthermore, the current law stipulates that labor in lieu of fines can be allowed with the consent of the individual, which is contrary to the purpose of property penalties. Therefore, this bill changes it to where labor in lieu of fines is not allowed unless the individual is unable to pay after compulsory enforcement.

XXI. If the criminal motive of a person sentenced to detention or a fine is clearly excusable for reasons of public interest or morality, there seems to be no need to execute the sentence. Therefore, this bill adds a provision allowing for a reprimand instead.

XXII. The current law stipulates that each two days of detention can be credited as one day of imprisonment, implying that the conditions in detention centers are superior to those in prisons. However, on-site inspections show that the facilities in detention centers are often inferior to those in prisons. As a result, those awaiting trial suffer even more than those who have been convicted. Therefore, this bill adopts a mandatory credit system and credits one day for one day.

XXIII. Issues such as how the effects of converting to fines, labor, or education relate to recidivism and probation are closely related. Therefore, this bill adds these provisions.

XXIV. The current law's articles on the execution of penalties in the Chapter on Penalties should be placed in the Criminal Procedure Law or the Prison Law. Therefore, this bill deletes them entirely.

XXV. The maliciousness of a recidivist is not necessarily directly proportional to the similarity or type of crime and the number of offenses. Therefore, this bill provides a general provision for aggravating the sentence for recidivists up to one-half, allowing judges to use discretion based on the circumstances.

XXVI. The circumstances of continuous offenses are sometimes extremely serious. Therefore, this bill specifically adds a provision for aggravating the sentence in such cases.

XXVII. The current law's provisions regarding fines focus on assessing the offender's financial resources and do not consider the benefits gained from the crime. As a result, the amount of the fine is often less than the benefits gained. Therefore, this bill grants judges the authority to increase the fine within the range of the benefits gained.

XXVIII. The crimes listed in Article 60 of this bill are all subject to simplified procedures under the Criminal Procedure Law. While prosecutors can make a decision not to prosecute, if the victim directly files a private prosecution with the court and the court finds the circumstances to be minor and clearly deserving of leniency, reducing the sentence seems insufficient. Therefore, this bill grants the court the power to exempt the sentence to maintain balance.

XXIX. The current law uniformly stipulates that self-reporting a crime results in a one-third reduction of the sentence, which is insufficient as an incentive. Therefore, this bill provides for general mitigation in the General Provisions and adds provisions for mitigating or exempting the sentence in the Special Provisions.

XXX. This bill stipulates that people under the age of 18 or over the age of 80 cannot be sentenced to death or life imprisonment. This is because those who are young can still be reformed, and those who are old should be treated with leniency. It is not appropriate to impose extreme penalties on either group.

XXXI. The current law sets two levels of mitigation: one-half and one-third. For cases where no specific fraction is provided, the mitigation is at least one-half, which is unfairly lenient. Furthermore, there are provisions for mitigating death and life sentences by fractions, which is theoretically flawed. Therefore, this bill clearly specifies the penalty ranges for mitigating death and life sentences and sets a general rule of reducing the sentence to one-half for mitigating imprisonment, detention, or fines. However, if there are provisions for exempting the sentence, the reduction can be up to one-third. It also clearly establishes applicable provisions for discretionary mitigation.

XXXII. The current law limits the conditions for probation to whether the offender has previously been sentenced. It does not include provisions for supervising those on probation, which seems inappropriate. Therefore, this bill changes it to where probation cannot be granted unless the judge believes that temporarily suspending the execution of the sentence is appropriate. It also stipulates that those sentenced to probation may be subject to protective supervision during the probation period.

XXXIII. Since the condition for parole is limited to having genuine evidence of remorse, the period of imprisonment need not be too long. Therefore, this bill changes the current law's "less than two years" to "less than one year."

XXXIV. The current law divides the statute of limitations for prosecution and execution of sentences into three types: 20 years, 10 years, and 3 years. This bill changes it to five types: 20 years, 10 years, 5 years, 3 years, and 1 year, which is more fair.

XXXV. The current law calculates the statute of limitations for prosecution from the date of the final act of the crime, which cannot include crimes that are in a continuous state except for continuous offenses. This bill specifically corrects this.

XXXVI. According to the current law, if the reason for suspending the statute of limitations has not disappeared, the statute of limitations will never be completed. Therefore, this bill specifically stipulates that the reason is deemed to have disappeared after a certain period.

XXXVII. The chapter count and titles in the Special Provisions section of the current law that have been added or revised in this bill are as follows:

(I) The articles in the Chapter on Offenses Against Elections only punish obstruction of elections, which is a somewhat narrow scope. This bill changes the chapter title to Chapter on Offenses Against Voting so that it can also apply to voting on initiatives, referendums, and recalls.

(II) The current law places counterfeiting of government bonds, company stocks, postage stamps, revenue stamps, and all other securities within the Chapter on Forgery of Documents and Seals, which seems inappropriate. This bill removes the articles on securities and creates a separate chapter.

(III) Profiteering and usury are extremely reprehensible. Therefore, this bill specifically adds punitive provisions to the Chapter on Fraud and Breach of Trust and changes the chapter title to Fraud, Breach of Trust, and Usury.

XXXVIII. If public officials who are derelict in their duties are not severely punished, there will never be clean governance. Therefore, in addition to appropriately increasing the number of articles on crimes committed by public officials, the punishment for public officials is uniformly increased.

XXXIX. Since the articles on relatives in the General Provisions section of the current law have been deleted, this bill clearly defines the scope of the articles on relatives in the Special Provisions section according to the circumstances to facilitate application.

XL. The current law aggravates the penalties for false accusations, violations of graves, corpses, abandonment, assault, and unlawful detention committed against lineal or collateral ascendants. This bill believes that the general penalties for the above crimes are already not light. If the circumstances of crimes against ascendants are serious, the maximum penalty of the original sentence can be imposed. There is no need to further aggravate the penalty. Therefore, only the articles on assault of lineal ascendants and violations of their graves and corpses are retained, and the rest are deleted.

XLI. The current law treats one's own property as another's property when it has been sealed or burdened by real rights, leased, or insured, in cases involving crimes of public danger and crimes of theft, robbery, extortion, embezzlement, fraud, breach of trust, and destruction of property. This bill believes that the Chapter on Public Danger already has punitive provisions for burning or flooding one's own property, and the Chapter on Obstructing Official Duties already has explicit punitive provisions for damaging or removing seals or markings affixed by public officials or acts that violate their validity. As for other situations, compensation for damages can be sought through civil law to provide redress. Therefore, Articles 209, 339, 359, and 385 of the current law are deleted.

XLII. Articles on causing death or serious injury in the current law mostly increase the penalties based on intentional injury, which involves repeated citations and is quite difficult to use. Therefore, this bill uniformly specifies the penalty ranges.

XLIII. Preparing to commit murder, robbery, or kidnapping for ransom is extremely dangerous. The current law does not punish such preparations, which seems inadequate. This bill adds punitive provisions.

XLIV. The current law limits the punishment for conspiracy to cases of murder, robbery, and kidnapping for ransom, which is too narrow. Furthermore, if there are instigating circumstances in a conspiracy, the provisions regarding instigation in the General Provisions can be applied. If there is only participation in the conspiracy, verbal assistance is a form of aiding, and the provisions regarding accomplices in the General Provisions can be applied. Therefore, this bill deletes Articles 288, 351, and 373 of the current law, which concern conspiracy.

XLV. Insurrection poses a minimal danger in its preparatory or conspiratorial stage. Punishments for those who turn themselves in can be relaxed. Therefore, this bill adds provisions for exemption from punishment.

XLVI. Article 105 of the current law, which stipulates aiding insurrection, is essentially about accomplices to insurrection, and provisions regarding accomplices in the General Provisions can be applied. Therefore, it is deleted.

XLVII. The current law only punishes those who violate government authorization when entering into treaties with foreign countries that harm sovereignty. This bill believes that those who have not received government authorization but privately enter into agreements with foreign governments or their representatives on matters that should be approved by the government should also be severely punished. Therefore, this bill adds this provision.

XLVIII. The offense in Article 112 of the current law is already included in Article 98 of this bill. Therefore, it is deleted.

XLIX. The penalties for ordinary intentional homicide, intentional injury, and unlawful detention are already quite severe. There is no need to further aggravate the penalties for committing the above crimes against heads of state of friendly nations. There is even less need to punish preparatory acts. As for crimes against foreign representatives, each has its own special article that can be applied based on its nature, and there is no need to apply the provisions of the articles on obstructing official duties. Therefore, this bill deletes Articles 121, 122, and 123 of the current law in the Chapter on Offenses Against National Relations. However, the ordinary punishment for publicly insulting heads of state of friendly nations and foreign representatives seems too light. Therefore, this bill adds an article specifying a more severe penalty.

L. Civilians privately colluding with the enemy in wartime are rare. As for soldiers, the Army, Navy, and Air Force Criminal Code can be applied. Therefore, Article 124 of the current law is deleted.

LI. Public officials who do not fulfill their duties and abandon their posts are guilty of heinous crimes. Therefore, this bill adds provisions for severe punishment.

LII. Bribery cases are often difficult to detect because the giver and receiver are equally guilty. Therefore, this bill deletes the offense of bribing public officials for actions within their duties. As for bribing public officials for actions that violate their duties, in addition to reducing the sentence, provisions are made for reducing or exempting the sentence for self-reporting and reducing the sentence for confessing to facilitate the detection of bribery cases.

LIII. Article 130 of the current law stipulates the special offense of bribery by public officials or arbiters with judicial duties. This bill increases the penalty for general bribery offenses. The public officials who are arbiters have now been changed to arbitrators and are specified in the relevant articles. Therefore, this article is deleted.

LIV. Article 133 of the current law only punishes public officials with the duty to prosecute crimes, which is somewhat narrow. Therefore, this bill adds public officials with the duty to punish crimes. Furthermore, abusing authority to arrest or detain is an extremely serious act that must be punished. Therefore, this bill adds provisions for this as well.

LV. Public officials who have custody, escort, or confinement of criminals who torture convicted or unconvicted criminal defendants or suspects are acting illegally. Therefore, this bill adds punitive provisions.

LVI. Public officials who accept civil or criminal lawsuits beyond their authority greatly impede the rule of law. Therefore, this bill adds punitive provisions.

LVII. Public officials who neglect their duties and cause disasters are unforgivable. Therefore, this bill adds punitive provisions.

LVIII. The current law does not have provisions for confiscating and recovering the value of direct or indirect gains for public officials who commit crimes of profiteering. This bill adds these provisions.

LIX. Article 137 of the current law punishes public officials who leak or deliver secrets and includes documents, drawings, information, and items related to domestic affairs of the Republic of China and documents, drawings, information, and items that should be kept secret other than for national defense. Furthermore, this bill believes that public officials who negligently leak or deliver secret documents, etc., other than for national defense, and non-public officials who leak or deliver secret documents, etc., other than for national defense, that they learned or possessed due to their duties or business should also be punished. Therefore, this bill adds these provisions.

LX. Examinations are a crucial matter for the state. If there is fraud that leads to inaccurate results, punishment should be imposed. Therefore, this bill adds these provisions.

LXI. Preventing crimes is the responsibility of the national police. Requiring the people to bear this responsibility is too harsh. Therefore, this bill deletes Articles 162 and 168 of the current law.

LXII. Instigating or soliciting lawsuits and profiting from them are reprehensible. Therefore, this bill adds punitive provisions.

LXIII. The current law only punishes perjury during court proceedings. It is impossible to prevent false statements during investigations. Therefore, this bill adds statements made during investigations, but only those made during investigations by prosecutors.

LXIV. Exposing corpses with infectious pathogens or spreading pathogens by other means can easily cause epidemics that greatly affect the lives and health of the people. Article 206 of the current law does not have provisions for this. Therefore, this bill adds this provision.

LXV. Most attempts to commit offenses related to the falsification of weights and measures are minor, and Article 221 of the current law is especially harsh in punishing possession based on the social conditions of our country. Therefore, they are all deleted. As for those who use weights and measures that violate the prescribed standards, the majority are those who are engaged in business. Therefore, this bill adds explicit provisions for more severe punishment.

LXVI. Article 232 of the current law limits the scope to doctors' certificates for those engaged in business who record untrue matters in documents created in the course of their business. Therefore, this bill expands the scope to all those engaged in business and all documents created in the course of their business to avoid omissions.

LXVII. The current law stipulates that all acts of sexual intercourse with girls under the age of 16 are treated as rape, which seems too strict considering the average development of girls and their ability to express consent. Therefore, this bill changes it to where sexual intercourse with girls under the age of 14 is treated as rape. Sexual intercourse with girls over the age of 14 but under the age of 16 is punished with a lighter sentence. The same provisions apply to indecent acts with boys or girls over the age of 14 but under the age of 16.

LXVIII. Article 256 of the current law only punishes married women who commit adultery, and does not punish married men who commit adultery, which is contrary to the principle of gender equality. Therefore, this bill punishes all those who commit adultery while married. At the same time, it stipulates that no accusation can be made unless there has been prior negotiation or a divorce judgment to maintain the peace of the family.

LXIX. The current law imposes the same punishment for enticing and abducting, which seems to be an imbalance of severity. Furthermore, it only limits it to those who have left the care of people with parental authority, guardians, or conservators, which is too narrow. This bill punishes abduction more severely than enticement and expands the scope to those who have left the care of all those with supervisory authority, which is more appropriate.

LXX. Enticing married women disrupts family organization. The current law does not have explicit punitive provisions, and many in the legal community have advocated for such provisions. Therefore, this bill adds this provision.

LXXI. Enticing boys and girls under the age of 16 is especially heinous. Therefore, this bill stipulates that it should be treated as abduction.

LXXII. Returning the enticed person or pointing out the location of the enticed person before the judgment is announced greatly benefits the victim. There is a need to reward this. Therefore, this bill adds provisions for reducing the sentence.

LXXIII. Obstructing the agricultural irrigation of others with the intention of harming them not only infringes on individual legal rights but also affects the rural economy. Therefore, this bill adds punitive provisions.

LXXIV. Falsely marking the country of origin or quality of goods deceives and damages commercial credit. Therefore, this bill adds explicit punitive provisions.

LXXV. The current law imposes the same punishment for manufacturing and selling opium, morphine, cocaine, heroin, and other narcotics. This bill believes that the harm to society from manufacturing and selling morphine, cocaine, heroin, and other narcotics is greater than that from manufacturing and selling opium. Therefore, it imposes separate punishments.

LXXVI. The current law specifies the penalties for those who premeditate murder, kill with cruel acts, and kill to facilitate or evade other crimes. This bill believes that ordinary murder can be punished with the death penalty. If the means of the crime and other circumstances are extremely heinous, the judge can consider everything and impose the death penalty. There is no need for separate provisions. Therefore, this bill deletes Articles 284 and 285 of the current law.

LXXVII. The current law only reduces the punishment of mothers who kill their children if the children are illegitimate, relative to ordinary murder. This bill believes that the nature of maternal love is inherently strong. Mothers will only kill their children if it is a matter of reputation, economic pressure, or other inevitable circumstances. Therefore, this bill stipulates that it is not limited to illegitimate children.

LXXVIII. Public health is related to the strength of the race. All those who transmit venereal disease to others, abuse young children, bind the feet of others, or otherwise impede the natural development of children's bodies should be punished. Therefore, this bill clearly specifies this.

LXXIX. The current law only punishes those who enslave people. However, there are often situations where people are not slaves in name but whose lack of freedom is similar to that of slaves, such as young children who perform in traveling shows and prostitutes raised by madams. All those who place people in such positions must be punished. Therefore, this bill adds this provision.

LXXX. Article 315 of the current law stipulates the offense of obstructing the freedom of women. This offense is less serious than Article 257, which obstructs both freedom and supervisory rights, yet the punishment is heavier, which seems inappropriate. Therefore, this bill revises this.

LXXXI. The current law does not have explicit punitive provisions for squatting on real property. This bill specifically adds an item to the Chapter on Theft so that the punishment for theft can be applied.

LXXXII. Committing kidnapping for ransom while also committing robbery or piracy is extremely serious and should be punished with extreme penalties. Therefore, this bill adds this provision.

Part 1 General Provisions

Chapter 1 Legal Precedents

Article 1 Punishment for an act is limited to explicit provisions in the law at the time of the act.

Article 2 If the law changes after an act, the law at the time of judgment shall apply. However, if the law prior to the judgment is more favorable to the actor, the law most favorable to the actor shall apply.

Security measures shall be appropriate for the law at the time of judgment.

If the law changes after a judgment of punishment has been finalized and the act is no longer punishable, the sentence shall be waived and its execution terminated.

Article 3 This law applies to those who commit crimes within the territory of the Republic of China. Those who commit crimes outside the territory of the Republic of China on a Republic of China vessel or aircraft shall be deemed to have committed the crime within the territory of the Republic of China.

Article 4 An act or result of a crime that occurs within the territory of the Republic of China shall be deemed to have been committed within the territory of the Republic of China.

Article 5 This law applies to those who commit the following crimes outside the territory of the Republic of China:

(1) Insurrection.

(2) Treason.

(3) Counterfeiting currency.

(4) Forgery of valuable securities as provided in Articles 201 and 202.

(5) Forgery of documents and seals as provided in Articles 211, 214, 216, and 218.

(6) Unlawful detention as provided in Article 296.

(7) Piracy as provided in Articles 333 and 334.

Article 6 This law applies to Republic of China public officials who commit the following crimes outside the territory of the Republic of China:

(1) Dereliction of duty as provided in Articles 121 through 123, 125, 126, 129, 131, 132, and 134.

(2) Escape as provided in Article 161.

(3) Forgery of documents as provided in Article 213.

(4) Embezzlement as provided in Article 336, paragraph 1.

Article 7 This law applies to citizens of the Republic of China who commit crimes other than those in the previous two articles outside the territory of the Republic of China, for which the minimum principal punishment is imprisonment for three years or more, except where the law of the place where the crime was committed does not punish such acts.

Article 8 The provisions of the preceding article shall apply mutatis mutandis to foreigners who commit crimes against citizens of the Republic of China outside the territory of the Republic of China.

Article 9 The same act may still be punished under this law, even if a final judgment has been rendered in a foreign country. However, if the whole or part of the sentence has been executed in a foreign country, the execution of the whole or part of the sentence may be waived.

Article 10 The terms "or more," "or less," and "within" shall include the stated number or penalty. The term "public official" refers to personnel who are legally engaged in public duties. The term "official document" refers to documents created by public officials in the course of their duties. The term "serious injury" refers to the following injuries:

(1) Destruction of vision in one or both eyes.

(2) Destruction of hearing in one or both ears.

(3) Destruction of speech, taste, or smell.

(4) Destruction of function in one or more limbs.

(5) Destruction of reproductive function.

(6) Other significant incurable or difficult-to-cure injuries to the body or health.

Article 11 This law also applies to the provisions of other laws and regulations that prescribe penalties, except where those other laws and regulations provide otherwise.

Chapter 2 Criminal Responsibility

Article 12 An act is not punishable if it is not the result of intent or negligence. Punishment for negligent acts is limited to cases where there is a specific provision.

Article 13 An actor who knows the facts constituting a crime and intends for it to occur is deemed to have intent.

An actor who foresees the facts constituting a crime occurring and does not believe its occurrence to be contrary to their will is deemed to have intent.

Article 14 An actor who is not intentional, but should have paid attention and could have paid attention according to the circumstances but did not, is deemed to have been negligent.

An actor who foresees the facts constituting a crime occurring but is confident that it will not occur is deemed to have been negligent.

Article 15 One who has a legal duty to prevent a certain result from occurring and can prevent it but does not, is the same as one who actively causes the result to occur.

One who, through their own actions, creates a risk of a certain result occurring has a duty to prevent its occurrence.

Article 16 One shall not be exempted from criminal responsibility due to ignorance of the law. However, the penalty may be reduced according to the circumstances. If one is confident that their act is permitted by law and has legitimate reasons, they may be exempted from punishment.

Article 17 If a crime causes a certain result to occur for which the penalty is increased, it shall not apply if the actor could not have foreseen its occurrence.

Article 18 Acts by persons under the age of fourteen shall not be punished.

Acts by persons fourteen years of age or older but under the age of eighteen may have their penalties reduced.

Acts by persons over the age of eighty may have their penalties reduced.

Article 19 Acts by persons who are mentally incapacitated shall not be punished.

Acts by persons who are mentally deficient may have their penalties reduced.

Article 20 Acts by persons who are deaf or mute may have their penalties reduced.

Article 21 Official actions taken under the orders of a superior public official shall not be punished, unless the order is known to be illegal.

Article 22 Legitimate business activities shall not be punished.

Article 23 Acts of defending one's own rights or the rights of others against an ongoing unlawful infringement shall not be punished. However, if the defensive act is excessive, the penalty may be reduced or waived.

Article 24 Acts that are unavoidable in order to avoid an imminent danger to one's own life, body, freedom, or property, or the life, body, freedom, or property of others shall not be punished. However, if the act of avoidance is excessive, the penalty may be reduced or waived.

The preceding provision regarding avoiding danger to oneself shall not apply to those with special obligations in public or business affairs.

Chapter 3 Attempted Offenses

Article 25 One who has commenced the execution of a criminal act but fails to complete it is an attempted offender.

Punishment for attempted offenses is limited to cases where there is a specific provision.

Article 26 The punishment for an attempted offense may be reduced based on the penalty for the completed offense. However, if the act cannot produce the result of the crime and is not dangerous, the penalty may be reduced or waived.

Article 27 One who has commenced the execution of a criminal act and voluntarily ceases or prevents the result from occurring shall have their penalty reduced or waived.

Chapter 4 Complicity

Article 28 Two or more persons who jointly commit a criminal act are all principal offenders.

Article 29 One who instigates another to commit a crime is an instigator.

Instigators shall be punished according to the crime they instigated.

Even if the person instigated does not commit the crime, the instigator shall still be treated as an attempted offender, but only if the crime instigated has provisions for punishing attempted offenses.

Article 30 One who assists another in committing a crime is an accomplice, even if the other person is unaware of the assistance.

The punishment for an accomplice may be reduced based on the penalty for the principal offender.

Article 31 For crimes that are constituted by status or other specific relationships, those who jointly commit, instigate, or assist in committing the crime shall still be punished for the crime, even if they do not have the specific relationship.

For crimes where the penalty is aggravated or waived due to status or other specific relationships, those who do not have the specific relationship shall be subject to the normal penalty.

Chapter 5 Penalties

Article 32 Penalties are divided into principal penalties and accessory penalties.

Article 33 The types of principal penalties are as follows:

(1) Death penalty.

(2) Life imprisonment.

(3) Imprisonment (two months or more, fifteen years or less, but when there is aggravation or mitigation, it may be reduced to less than two months or increased to twenty years).

(4) Detention (one day or more, less than two months, but when there is aggravation, it may be increased to four months).

(5) Fine (one yuan or more).

Article 34 The types of accessory penalties are as follows:

(1) Deprivation of public rights.

(2) Confiscation.

Article 35 The severity of the principal penalties is determined by the order specified in Article 33.

For the same type of penalty, the one with the longer or greater maximum is more severe. If the maximums are equal, the one with the longer or greater minimum is more severe.

Apart from the provisions of the preceding two paragraphs, the severity of the penalty is determined with reference to the standards of the preceding two paragraphs. If it cannot be determined according to the standards of the preceding two paragraphs, it shall be determined according to the circumstances of the crime.

Article 36 Deprivation of public rights entails the deprivation of the following qualifications:

1. The qualification to be a public official.

2. The qualification to be a candidate for public office.

3. The qualification to exercise the four rights of election, recall, initiative, and referendum.

Article 37 One who is sentenced to death or life imprisonment shall be sentenced to deprivation of public rights for life.

One who is sentenced to imprisonment for six months or more and is deemed to require deprivation of public rights based on the nature of the crime shall be sentenced to deprivation of public rights for one to ten years.

Deprivation of public rights shall be pronounced concurrently with the judgment.

Deprivation of public rights declared according to the first paragraph shall take effect from the time the judgment becomes final. Deprivation of public rights declared according to the second paragraph shall be calculated from the date of completion of the execution of the principal punishment or pardon.

Article 38 The following items shall be confiscated:

1. Contraband.

2. Items used in the commission of a crime or prepared for the commission of a crime.

3. Items obtained

Article 333 Whoever, without the permission of a belligerent nation or not belonging to the navy of any nation, pilots a vessel with the intent to use violence or coercion against another vessel or the persons or property thereon, shall be deemed guilty of piracy and shall be punished with death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for not less than seven years. If crew members or passengers, with the intent to plunder property or use violence or coercion against other crew members or passengers, pilot or command a vessel, they shall be treated as pirates.

If the act results in death, the punishment shall be death; if it results in serious injury, the punishment shall be death or life imprisonment.

Article 334 Whoever commits piracy and commits any of the following acts shall be punished with death:

(1) Arson;

(2) Rape;

(3) Kidnapping for ransom;

(4) Intentional homicide.

Page 20

Chapter 31 Embezzlement

Article 335 Whoever, with the intent to illegally possess for himself or a third party, embezzles an object held by himself that belongs to another, shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than five years, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan, or both.

An attempt to commit the crime described in the preceding paragraph shall also be punished.

Article 336 Whoever commits the crime described in the first paragraph of the preceding article with respect to an object held in public service or for public benefit shall be punished with imprisonment for not less than one year and not more than seven years, and may also be fined not more than five thousand yuan.

Whoever commits the crime described in the first paragraph of the preceding article with respect to an object held in the course of business shall be punished with imprisonment for not less than six months and not more than five years, and may also be fined not more than three thousand yuan.

An attempt to commit the crime described in the preceding two paragraphs shall also be punished.

Article 337 Whoever, with the intent to illegally possess for himself or a third party, embezzles a lost item, a floating object, or any other object separated from the possession of its owner, shall be punished with a fine of not less than five hundred yuan.

Article 338 The provisions of Articles 323 and 324 shall apply mutatis mutandis to the crimes in this chapter.

Chapter 32 Fraud, Breach of Trust, and Usury

Article 339 Whoever, with the intent to illegally possess for himself or a third party, uses fraudulent means to induce a person to deliver an object belonging to himself or a third party, shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than five years, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan, or both.

The same shall apply to anyone who obtains an illegal benefit in property by the means described in the preceding paragraph, or causes a third party to obtain such a benefit.

An attempt to commit the crime described in the preceding two paragraphs shall also be punished.

Article 340 Whoever habitually commits the crime described in the preceding article shall be punished with imprisonment for not less than one year and not more than seven years, and may also be fined not more than five thousand yuan.

Article 341 Whoever, with the intent to illegally possess for himself or a third party, takes advantage of a person under the age of twenty's inexperience or a person's mental weakness to induce him to deliver an object belonging to himself or a third party, shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than five years, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan, or both.

The same shall apply to anyone who obtains an illegal benefit in property by the means described in the preceding paragraph, or causes a third party to obtain such a benefit.

An attempt to commit the crime described in the preceding two paragraphs shall also be punished.

Article 342 Whoever, in handling affairs for another person, with the intent to obtain illegal benefits for himself or a third party, or to harm the interests of the principal, acts in violation of his duty, causing damage to the property or other interests of the principal, shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than five years, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan, or both.

An attempt to commit the crime described in the preceding paragraph shall also be punished.

Article 343 The provisions of Articles 323 and 324 shall apply mutatis mutandis to the crimes described in the preceding four articles.

Article 344 Whoever, taking advantage of another person's urgent need, carelessness, or lack of experience, lends money or other items and obtains an excessively high interest rate that is clearly disproportionate to the principal, shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than one year, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan, or both.

Article 345 Whoever habitually commits the crime described in the preceding article shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than five years, and may also be fined not more than three thousand yuan.

Chapter 33 Intimidation and Kidnapping for Ransom

Article 346 Whoever, with the intent to illegally possess for himself or a third party, uses intimidation to induce a person to deliver an object belonging to himself or a third party, shall be punished with imprisonment for not less than six months and not more than five years, and may also be fined not more than one thousand yuan.

The same shall apply to anyone who obtains an illegal benefit in property by the means described in the preceding paragraph, or causes a third party to obtain such a benefit.

An attempt to commit the crime described in the preceding two paragraphs shall also be punished.

Article 347 Whoever kidnaps a person with the intent to demand a ransom shall be punished with death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for not less than seven years.

If the act results in death or serious injury, the punishment shall be death or life imprisonment. An attempt to commit the crime described in the first paragraph shall also be punished.

Whoever prepares to commit the crime described in the first paragraph shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than two years. Whoever commits the crime described in the first paragraph and releases the victim without receiving a ransom may have his punishment reduced.

Article 348 Whoever commits the crime described in the first paragraph of the preceding article and intentionally kills the victim shall be punished with death.

Whoever commits the crime described in the first paragraph of the preceding article and rapes the victim shall be punished with death or life imprisonment.

Chapter 34 Receiving Stolen Goods

Article 349 Whoever receives stolen goods shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than three years, detention, or a fine of not more than five hundred yuan.

Whoever transports, hides, knowingly purchases stolen goods, or acts as a broker for stolen goods shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than five years, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan, or both.

Property acquired from stolen goods shall be deemed stolen goods.

Article 350 Whoever habitually commits the crime described in the preceding article shall be punished with imprisonment for not less than six months and not more than five years, and may also be fined not more than three thousand yuan.

Article 351 If the crime in this chapter is committed between lineal relatives, spouses, or relatives living together in the same household, the punishment may be waived.

Chapter 35 Destruction and Damage

Article 352 Whoever destroys or damages another person's documents or renders them unusable, and such act is sufficient to cause damage to the public or another person, shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than three years, detention, or a fine of not more than five hundred yuan.

Article 353 Whoever destroys another person's building, mine, ship, pit, or warship, or renders it unusable, shall be punished with imprisonment for not less than six months and not more than five years.

If the act results in death, the punishment shall be life imprisonment or imprisonment for not less than seven years; if it results in serious injury, the punishment shall be imprisonment for not less than three years and not more than ten years.

An attempt to commit the crime described in the first paragraph shall also be punished.

Article 354 Whoever destroys or damages another person's object other than those described in the preceding two articles, or renders it unusable, and such act is sufficient to cause damage to the public or another person, shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than two years, detention, or a fine of not more than five hundred yuan.

Article 355 Whoever, with the intent to harm another person, uses fraudulent means to cause himself or a third party to make a disposition of property, thereby causing damage to property, shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than three years, detention, or a fine of not more than five hundred yuan.

Article 356 A debtor who, at the time of being subjected to compulsory execution, with the intent to harm the rights of his creditor, destroys, disposes of, or conceals his property shall be punished with imprisonment for not more than two years, detention, or a fine of not more than five hundred yuan.

Article 357 The crimes described in Articles 352 and 354 to 356 shall be prosecuted only upon complaint. (End)

Free Talk

Chrysanthemums and Tao Yuanming

— Yao Tianyu

Autumn deepens, and the chrysanthemums of the eastern fence are all blooming with their rare and beautiful flowers, exuding their cool fragrance, decorating the autumn sky, appearing extremely refined and beautiful.

Other flowers flaunt their charms to people in the spring and summer seasons with a flamboyant and alluring attitude, but only the chrysanthemum appears in this late autumn season. Even under the oppression of harsh wind and frost, it will not yield. This shows its aloofness and extraordinary spirit.

Because of the chrysanthemum's aloofness and striving spirit, I thought of Tao Yuanming.

He was a poet with a backbone of pride, his thoughts were lofty, and his character was outstanding. When he was serving as "Magistrate of Pengze," one day, a supervisor was going to see him. Someone advised him to put on his official robes and pay his respects, but he arrogantly retorted, "I cannot bend my waist for five pecks of rice!" So he abandoned his official position and returned to his homeland.

He had no fondness for other flowers, only a special love for chrysanthemums. Perhaps it was because the chrysanthemum's character coincided with his temperament? Although his homeland was desolate, the chrysanthemums he planted filled the garden. Although he was unemployed and lived a simple life, he was very "contented and at ease" with the chrysanthemums as his companions, drinking his wine, and writing his poems.

Now, when people talk about appreciating chrysanthemums, they must also flaunt a so-called "Yuanming obsession." But how many people today can possess the same lofty thoughts and outstanding character as him? Many people are desperately flattering dignitaries to seek promotion, or they are selling their own valuable personality and soul to be tools and running dogs for others to command. These vulgar people can just appreciate the chrysanthemums if they want to (but if the chrysanthemums had feelings, they might not welcome these people to "appreciate" them, right?). Why bother to disgrace Mr. Tao's noble reputation?

Crab Feast Under Red Maple Leaves

— Huang Qingbai

When the reed catkins turn old and white, the maple leaves become drunk and red. Standing quietly at the gate of the thatched cottage, the wind from the fields paints the clear scenery with a layer of greyish-brown. Looking at the car like a black ox on the road, it evokes the emotion of missing friends - "Are you tired of the city? On Sunday afternoon, I'll set up a crab feast for you under the red maple leaves. The chrysanthemums are especially yellow this year, come on." -

On the fifth day after the pink invitation was brought by the postman, six city dwellers with the smell of coal smoke were sitting around in a low, old-fashioned skylight hall, talking and laughing, as if they had all forgotten their own homes. The city dwellers sat under the red maple leaves and argued about the types of chrysanthemums. The crabs had already changed into their red guest-greeting attire in the black iron pot.

"Drink as much as you can, twilight is the time to be drunk. I'll prepare a sweet betel leaf soup for you," my wife said, wearing a white apron over her dark cheongsam, with her hair in a hurried mess and a sweet smile on her face. As the crab shells were being peeled, friends began to shower me with envious words, "Happiness!" They didn't care that the red maple leaves were falling one by one, only drinking the mellow wheat shochu.

"Tearing these crabs apart is like tearing oneself apart for those who are not happy. Isn't one being torn apart and eaten by others?" a friend said, filled with deep sorrow. But "Why be so sentimental? Look, when the maple leaves fall, aren't the chrysanthemums blooming? The crabs are inexhaustible, they still have claws that can pinch people." In the rose-colored twilight, the red maple leaves turned purple, and everyone felt a chill.

Chrysanthemum Obsession

— Jin Xiongyu

Seeing other people's potted chrysanthemums, I was reminded of the interesting story of Mr. Zhang's chrysanthemum obsession in my hometown. Chrysanthemums sprout from dormant roots in spring, are divided and transplanted in summer, and bloom in late autumn. There are many varieties. "Li Shizhen said there are nine hundred varieties." They are roughly divided into two types: those with purple stems, fragrant aroma, and sweet taste are true chrysanthemums, for the enjoyment of poets and writers; those with green stems, a mugwort-like aroma, and a bitter taste are commonly called wild chrysanthemums, used for medicinal purposes.

Mr. Zhang, surnamed Zhang, is already in his seventies, full of vigor. Besides poetry and books, he has a mania for growing chrysanthemums. Every year, he plants as many as a thousand pots. The variety and refinement of his cultivation are the best in the county. Behind his house, there is a vacant lot, which he has turned into a garden, surrounded by a fence. Passersby often see Mr. Zhang bending over on the chrysanthemum path, supporting and nurturing them in every way. He also hires two workers to specialize in moving, transporting, and irrigating. The garden gate is heavily guarded, and only those with similar voices and interests can enter.

I have had a family friendship with Mr. Zhang for generations, and I get to visit him from time to time. I remember last year today, when the flowers were blooming all over the garden, the fragrance of the flowers filled the room, and offerings were placed on the altar in the hall, which was quite elegant. So I invited friends and companions to gather together, holding crab claws with wine cups, and making a pair with the birthday celebrant in the scenery. Soon, wine glasses were exchanged, some recited poetry, and some painted pictures, the joy was boundless. Some of the guests who were of the same background, continued to linger and examine the chrysanthemums in detail. At the time, Mr. Zhang also left his seat, following the guests on both sides, guarding against any elegant acts that might lead to the dispersal of good varieties. I thought there might be suspicion of impropriety, so I stood by with my hands in my sleeves and offered congratulations.

In the autumn of the thirteenth year of the Republic, during the dispute over the fast, troops were stationed in my hometown for several days, and we also suffered from it. Among the military officers, there was one who liked chrysanthemums. He passed by Mr. Zhang's garden, just as the chrysanthemums were beginning to bloom. So he entered the garden with his guards, selected a few of the best varieties, and took them away. When Mr. Zhang found out, he was filled with anger, saying that a scholar could be humiliated, but flowers could not be insulted. He quickly chased after them, shouting and running, even though he was sweating profusely, he did not give up. When the military officer saw his pitiful state, he was moved by compassion and returned the flowers to him with a smile. To this day, it is still told as a pleasant story, and everyone calls him Duke Chrysanthemum.

Ways to Eat Crab

— (Lu Shifang)

(1) Fried Crab: Place the crab in a pot, add a little water, and cook it thoroughly. When eating, add soy sauce and shredded ginger, which is extremely delicious. This method of cooking is very simple and best preserves the true flavor of the crab, but it is best to use large crabs.

(2) Soy Sauce Crab: Cut a crab in half along the navel, coat it with flour, put it in a frying pan and fry it, then add soy sauce, wine, etc., and simmer for a while until cooked. It is also very delicious to eat, but it is slightly greasy.

(3) Stewed Crab: Break off the crab's claws and legs, put them in a bowl with the torso, add a little soy sauce and wine, and steam in a pot until cooked. The taste is quite delicious.

(4) Drunken Crab: Soak a smaller crab in wine (it must be thoroughly soaked), store it in a jar, and seal the mouth. After a few days, take it out and eat it, which has a different flavor.

(5) Crab Meat: After frying the crab, peel off the meat and fat, which is called crab meat. If you stir-fry it with shredded pork or tofu, it tastes very delicious.

Talking About Chrysanthemums

— Wu Yuanzhai

In previous years, on my late father's banner, there was a poem about chrysanthemums by Zhu Yuanzhang, which I saw often when I was young, so I memorized it well, and I still remember it today. The poem says: "A hundred flowers bloom, I do not bloom, if I bloom, all will be startled. I want to fight a battle with the west wind, and wear a golden armor all over my body." It is a poem about yellow chrysanthemums. Zhou Maoshu called the chrysanthemum the hermit among flowers. Tao Jingjie was originally a noble hermit, and his nature was close to it, so he loved chrysanthemums alone and regarded them as his confidants. However, since Zhu Yuanzhang, a feudal monarch, wrote chrysanthemum poems, they contained imperial ideas, which overflowed in his words. Zhu Yuanzhang was originally a rogue commoner, who leaped to the throne and became an emperor. Success meant he was a king, failure meant he was a bandit. After he became emperor, he later became suspicious of scholars, suspecting that writing meant plotting rebellion, and suspecting that saying "sheng" (生, meaning to be born) meant saying "seng" (僧, meaning monk), suspecting that people were scolding him for having been a thief and a monk. Using homophonic characters, he committed a great taboo and started an unnecessary literary inquisition, killing many innocent officials. His line "wear a golden armor all over my body" is the same tone as Xiang Yu's words when he saw Qin Shihuang on his tour, "He can be replaced." In the world, any kind of thing has its own psychological effect on the observer, as the saying goes, "The benevolent see it as benevolence, the wise see it as wisdom, is it only true of chrysanthemums?"

There are indeed many people who love chrysanthemums now, but how many can be called confidants of chrysanthemums in terms of character and integrity? Human desires are rampant, and there are indeed many who harbor thoughts of wealth and honor, even seeking "wealth and honor through injustice." The peony is a flower of wealth and honor, and there are really many people who can be confidants with peonies. The true confidants of chrysanthemums are probably not as many as that. "The most difficult thing in life is to find a confidant," not only is it true of people, but chrysanthemums also have such sympathy.

Previously, in a certain newspaper, I saw an article that overturned the case, cursing chrysanthemums, saying that chrysanthemums are opportunists and have a pungent odor, simply saying that chrysanthemums have no value at all. Such sharp writing cannot be called "a wonderful article that promotes the old and brings forth the new." But I really feel wronged for chrysanthemums!

Cursing chrysanthemums is originally a playful joke, so I realized that people who are "isolated and unsociable" run into walls everywhere. Even though there is no reason to scold them, they still want to think of some words to curse and exclude them!

— Yi An

All Kinds of Crabs

— Yan Beguang

Time flies so fast, in the blink of an eye it is time for red maples to be dyed with rouge, and yellow chrysanthemums to burst into bloom. Most poets and writers will enjoy themselves in time, holding crabs and facing the chrysanthemums, old autumns and fat crabs are the first delicacies of the season.

I remember when I was working in Suzhou, because the Yangcheng Lake crabs had long been well-known, I had the tea servant buy two every night for a quick meal. But I could never buy the ones with golden claws and yellow hair. It is said that Yangcheng Lake crabs are different from other producing areas, with golden claws and yellow hair. When placed on a gold-lacquered table, they crawl quickly on their bellies, and their feet are strong.

A friend told me that even the people of Suzhou cannot eat the real Yangcheng Lake crabs. They are all transported and sold in Shanghai, and I secretly sighed that the people of Shanghai have insatiable appetites!

Once, several colleagues in the bureau were happily discussing, and they held a crab-eating competition. A total of eighteen people signed up to participate. It was held at the He Garden in Hanji Lane. The scenery of He Garden is very good, taking full advantage of the beauty of the garden!

The rules of the competition were that whoever ate the fastest, the cleanest, and the most would be the first place and would be rewarded with a silver wine cup. As a result, Mr. Ge Yunyun took the first place, spending three hours and ten minutes, eating ninety-two crabs. Everyone admired his exquisite way of eating. By midnight, he had a stomach ache like a pattern, and he hurriedly asked Dr. Wu Guangmin to give him an enema, and Mr. Gu Xuanru examined his pulse. Although he got the silver cup, it was not worth it. After all, the nature of crabs is too cold, and you should not eat too many.

Crabs are crustaceans in the water, and their nature is very cold. The way to eat crabs is to first use a brush to wash away the mud on their bodies in clean water. The dirt on the hairs of the two claws is even more dirty and must be washed clean. Squeeze out the crab dirt from the navel, embed a slice of ginger, a few grains of salt, and tie it with hemp thread. Put clean water in the pot, about an inch from the water surface, place a bamboo steamer, buy three coppers of perilla in a Chinese medicine shop, wash it clean, spread it flat, put the crab on the perilla, and boil the water, then simmer for a while. If there is a poisonous crab inside, the crab shell will crack open when it sees the smell of perilla. When eating, it is best to use ginger powder to mix Zhenjiang rose vinegar, but it is also good to put it in a bowl, add aged wine, soy sauce, salt, ginger, and stew it. There are also those who cut the crab in half, mix it with flour, and fry it in a frying pan, which is called fried crab, but it is not as delicious as steaming.

There are crab raincoats on both sides of the crab's belly. Take them off when they are hot, and rub them vigorously a dozen times on the scars of hands and feet that have been frostbitten, and by winter, no matter how cold the weather is, the hands and feet will no longer suffer from frostbite. I wish the modern girls who wear long silk stockings to try it out! I guarantee that it will definitely work.

There is a crab monk inside the crab's belly, which is very cold in nature. Eating it can easily make people sick. Friends who eat crab should pay attention.

Crabs and persimmons are contradictory. It is recorded in detail in the Materia Medica, because both are cold in nature, if you accidentally eat them, it will make your stomach hurt even more. If you accidentally feel a stomach ache after eating crabs, you can boil four cents of longan meat in soup and take it, and the pain can be stopped immediately.

The crab season is not long, September and October are the most seasonal, so there is a popular saying that nine are pointed and ten are round, especially in mid-October is the best time, regardless of male or female, they are all fat and full of brains. However, use a small jar, spread some grains on the bottom of the jar, then put the crab in, and then cover the crab with grains to fill it, it can be stored for two months, and when you take it out to eat, it tastes especially delicious. After eating, it is best to wash your hands with chrysanthemum leaves to avoid the fishy smell.

When crabs are on the market, I buy three crabs every one or two days, two round and one pointed, and go to the restaurant to supervise the waiter to wash them clean, sprinkle perilla in the steaming basket, put the crabs in, steam them hot, and eat them hot with foreign vinegar, drinking one and a half catties of wine. For the remaining crab legs, I ask the waiter to take apart the crab meat and stir-fry a bowl of crab meat and egg rice with two eggs, which feels very comfortable to eat.

Pregnant women should not eat crabs, because they are cold in nature, and crab claws are prone to miscarriage, so be careful! It is popularly said that eating crabs during pregnancy will cause the child to have a lot of saliva and not stop flowing, but this cannot be confirmed. Leave the crab shell until summer, grind it into powder, then add dried and ground pomfret bones, mix it evenly with sawdust, and put it in a paper tube, which is a good mosquito incense.
