Special Article

Further Discussion on the Form and Legacy of Art

— Xin Ren

I was very happy to see the disagreement raised by Mr. "Ye" on the 18th of October on my article in this publication. Indeed, "if the literary world is polite and has no debate," "that would be a sign of literary death." However, I cannot quickly access the news magazines in China and cannot conduct our discussion quickly, which I greatly regret.

Mr. "Ye" first pointed out that the words I said in the first paragraph of the article "The Form and Legacy of Art" have a place that "can easily lead people to this misunderstanding," "that is, to think that it is not the content that determines the form, but the writer's style in the process of artistically processing the realistic material that he has captured."

Here, if my clumsy words cannot fully express my meaning and cause the readers to have such a misunderstanding, then I fully accept Mr. "Ye's" criticism, except for the last sentence (which we will talk about later). But what I said there was this: "In art, the main expression of form lies in the writer's style." This may be the root cause of the misunderstanding. Of course, form and content "have an inseparable legal law." The artist's unique style is determined and formed by the social conditions in which the artist is located, as well as the artist's social life, etc. Different social conditions and different social lives make even artists who are born in the same era and the same society have different artistic styles. Even writers from the same social stratum have different styles due to their different talents and experiences. Therefore, although we cannot confuse the form of art works with the writer's style, many of the basic elements that determine the two things are common. It is obvious that style cannot completely determine form, because they are both determined by something more fundamental. But can we deny the close and inseparable connection between style and form? When we read Shakespeare's plays, in that form (of course, independent of the content), do we not first notice the bold and unique style? If my previous sentence is understood in this sense, perhaps it would not cause misunderstanding. Moreover, I went on to say: "The artist's primary task is to capture the content of art from reality, and secondly..." Compared with what Mr. "Ye" said, "The so-called artistic expression form of the writer is expressed as a secondary thing here. What becomes the first thing in the writer's artistic creation process is the writer's attitude towards reality...", I feel that except for the expression of my clumsy words that should be criticized, it is difficult to find a contrary point in the content.

Mr. "Ye" also confused the contradiction between the worldview and the objective historical development, as well as the contradiction between the worldview and the method of creation. And I think that the contradiction between the worldview and the objective development of history is caused by the fact that the consciousness and demands of the social group that determines and creates the worldview violate the objective development of history. And what else is there to solve all contradictions, except to practice them in practice? But this is a general statement. We must not forget: what we are talking about now is art—we are talking about the artist's worldview and method of creation!

Historical facts fully prove it to us. Why does a writer whose worldview and method of creation are contradictory, slowly and circuitously make his worldview tend to objective reality: while another kind of the same writer does not have this phenomenon. Except for saying that the former has the practice of a realistic method of creation, but the latter does not (of course he also "creates", but that is far from reality, not the meaning of "creative practice" that we are talking about), how else can we explain this? Please see what Mr. "Ye" said: "Balzac and Tolstoy's consciousness violated history. Because of this, they did not fully grasp the unity of worldview and method of creation. It is this that restricted their development and the fluctuating consciousness expressed in their works. However, this still does not prevent them from becoming a realist." Here, Mr. "Ye" did not explain to us at all how Balzac, etc., would achieve a great realist from "a fluctuating consciousness that violates history"; that "however" cannot be used as a bridge from the former to the latter.

Finally, Mr. "Ye" repeatedly mentioned "the imitation of style." I repeat, this "sudden change" statement is the easiest way to make our discussion scattered and divergent. I said that it is "very worthy of our attention and taste" and "cannot be ignored," I did not say anything about imitating style. The writer's style, as mentioned earlier, is formed by the writer's social life, talent, etc. It is a common phenomenon for people who are just learning to write to imitate the style of other writers, but this is temporary.

I agree that inheriting the legacy of great classical writers is "related to the whole of the classical writer's method of creation." But I specifically pointed out the comprehensive form of art. Why? Because this point is "very worthy of our attention and taste." When studying this issue, how to synthesize and what to synthesize is the focus of our attention. We want to study the creative methods of classical writers in that kind of comprehensive and bold form. If this is "making the problem too narrow," I would rather "narrow it down."

Coming Home (Continuation)

— Wu Yan

At that time, I felt that this person was a bit strange. On one hand, I liked him, but on the other hand, I was also wary of him. I originally wanted to buy an overcoat to shield myself from the December cold, but I was afraid of encountering the ridiculous story in the sermons of Reverend Wakefield about Moses going to the market to sell a horse and buy spectacles. So, I simply bought some other cotton clothes. When I found out that he did not go ashore with the hawkers after leaving Hong Kong, I completely thought of him as just a kind-hearted travel companion. A fellow traveler, as long as you recognize that he is kind-hearted and not essentially bad, even if he makes you unhappy at times, you will gradually forgive him and get along with him completely. Therefore, I also started to chat enthusiastically with this travel companion who was in the habit of agreeing with others, and he certainly had the ability to make people enjoy talking with him.

While we were talking, his right hand was unconsciously groping inside his overcoat pocket. When I was shaking off the coal dust from my clothes (which I had to do almost every half hour), his hand came out of his pocket, along with a roll of red paper printed with regular script characters. He first looked at me with those pleasing eyes before carefully handing me a piece. It said: "Our shop has a three-story Western-style building facing the sea, with electric lights and fans, fully equipped, serving food and drinks, considerate and inexpensive..."

"Please be sure to stay at our shop when you come to Xiamen!"

What else was there to say? We had just been talking so happily, so of course, I agreed. Besides, I would have to stay at a hotel anyway. After I agreed, he wrapped his overcoat even more tightly and hurried away. I remained, watching the savage night engulf the sea and sky and the affairs of the world, listening to the bold sounds of foreign flags and wind and waves mingling together.

I returned to where I was staying and saw the same red paper strips pasted on the tin trunks and bamboo baskets. Other people's luggage was also pasted with the same. A sailor sitting next to me smoking saw me looking and flicked the ash off his cigarette, saying:

"This shop is not bad—no matter how many days you stay, the room rate is only three dollars, it's really fair and honest!"

On the Indian Ocean, the deck was full of people, both day and night. Now that we were on the Pacific Ocean, some of the passengers had already disembarked in Hong Kong, and the rest had been driven below deck by the cold mist and wind. So, the empty deck was left to the sailors to sell fried noodles and snacks. I put my hands in my trouser pockets and strolled around as if I were visiting a night market, with a very leisurely attitude.

"Hey, have a drink!"

I looked up and saw that it was the hotel solicitor who was greeting me. He was happily drinking with some people next to where the crane was placed, and the sailor who had just spoken to me was also sitting with them.

When the ship docked in the port of Xiamen, the greeters from other hotels swarmed onto the ship, vying to fly various leaflets at us, shouting the names of various hotels. He, the one who often flashed gentle glances at people, used his thumb and middle finger to make a clicking sound in front of their faces, saying:

"Sorry! They're all posted!"

The others seemed a little afraid of him and quickly walked away. He called a small boat to take our group of guests ashore, and then the three-and-a-half-story Western-style building, very old, appeared. Inside, there were no electric fans or separate small rooms, only beds with mats, disgustingly surrounding us one after another. Looking out from the window with missing glass panes, the pier with vehicles coming and going and the harbor with masts standing like forests were not far in front of the shop.

"Hurry up, or do you want me to skin you?"

He had just scolded a porter like that when he suddenly saw another porter drop the two rolls of bedding he was carrying on his shoulder onto the floor. He threw the sun helmet off his head onto the table, rolled up the sleeves of his coat, and shouted fiercely:

"I'll beat you to death!"

But he didn't actually hit him, it seemed like he was just trying to scare him. However, the entire shop was filled with his piercing voice, which would make a traveler who had spent half a month at sea, wanting to rest for a while, feel extremely unhappy. So, like several other guests, I stayed for a while and wanted to change hotels. He ran over with a smile, still flashing his ingratiating eyes, saying:

"Okay, okay, but the three dollars for the room must be paid, whether you stay or not. This is the old rule!"

He spoke the last words very harshly, as if the old rule was the law. At the same time, he looked at our boxes and baskets, which already had another piece of paper pasted on them. Although the color was the same, what was written was completely different, and it matched the contents of his shop exactly. We didn't want to stay, and we didn't want to cause trouble with him, so we gave him three dollars as he said. Even though we encountered such an unpleasant thing, it was still pleasant and happy to be stepping on our own land. But the next day on Gulangyu, when I saw the same big turbans, the same wooden sticks, and the same brown faces that I had seen in Yangon, Singapore, and Hong Kong, I once again felt a huge palm, invisibly covering my head, and a heavy tropical depression rose in my heart again.

November Street

— Shen Shengshi

The November street, flowing with a biting northwest wind, the market town is desolate, the shop is broadcasting a trembling song on the radio.

The farmers who go to market together, carrying baskets, folding their hands, their hungry eyes staring straight into the shop, and some are hesitating at the pawnshop door with clothes wrapped.

I walked quietly on the street, and returned quietly, lost in thought, at the bridgehead at the turn, I suddenly met a friend I hadn't seen for a long time.

—When did you come back?

—Just three days.

—Are you happy there?

But unexpectedly, my friend's face sank, and he froze for a moment.

—Coming back, everything is over!

—Oh… Is it?

—I had a small job in a company, but the company closed down!

—Then where are you going?

Without answering, I saw that his face was cramped, as if he couldn't answer a word to me?

—Old ×, what about you?

I smiled bitterly to myself and shook my head.

It's like all the words have been said.

—Old ×, it's getting cold!

—It's getting cold!

His feet rubbed against the ground, and he was about to leave.

—Where are you going?

—…Just walking around, he put his hands in his pockets, and walked away, his shoulders shrugging.

I stood under the bridgehead and watched his back, I thought of the pawnshop on the Zhongshi Street section of the bridge.

The November street, flowing with a biting northwest wind, I carried a lost sorrow, and went back silently.

Scenery of Peiping (One-Act Comedy) (Two)

— Xu Xu

Bu: You little brat! Humph! Old Han, I believe she wouldn't really go kiss her. —Old Han, right? This guy, I just don't believe you!

Liu: I don't want women! If I wanted to, I could get a dozen!

Han: Old Liu, let's help him this time! If it fails today, then he can only blame himself for being stupid, don't blame us for not helping a friend! If it succeeds, and we don't all go out to eat, then I'll definitely harm you!

Bu: Good! Now let's move things!

(So they start to move. Old Liu exits, and returns a moment later.)

Liu: (Carrying a plank) Old Han, come on, let's move this first, the drummer (Note 1) has already been arranged!

Han: (Carrying a plank) Good! Old Bu, you carry the bench!

(Liu and Han carry the plank and are about to exit, the shopkeeper enters,)

Shopkeeper: Mr. Han, are you going to sell the plank?

Liu: Aren't you asking us to pay the rent?

Shopkeeper: Are you going to sell my things to pay me back? Then wouldn't I sell them myself?

Liu: Didn't you say you wanted to spend the money?

Shopkeeper: Yes!

Liu: Then wouldn't it be better to sell it to you for money? When we have money, we'll buy a new one to return to you. Anyway, it's we who sleep on it, not you!

Shopkeeper: How much are you selling it for?

Liu: Two dollars.

Shopkeeper: That's still far from enough to pay me the rent!

Liu: Didn't you say to pay you one or two dollars first?

Once the abandoned fields are finally determined, the production may be less than what is currently indicated. The winter wheat production estimate is 386 million bushels, so this year's wheat production will be 466 million, and domestic demand is estimated to account for 650 million ○

Recently, there have been inquiries about how to calculate the difference in the rise and fall of foreign wheat in the newspaper's wheat market news, and what unit is used for the Chicago wheat market. The answer is as follows: The degree of rise and fall of foreign wheat in the wheat market news is calculated by converting the foreign wheat market into a ton to calculate the difference. For example, if the Chicago wheat price was 95.25 on the previous day and 97.75 on this day, and rose by 2.25, this is the price of one American bushel. Thirty-three American bushels are one ton, then multiply it by 33, that is, one ton of American wheat rose 54.25 US cents compared to the previous day. The Chicago wheat market is priced per bushel (commonly known as American bushel, abbreviated as bushel), and the price is in US dollars "cents".

Interbank lending still opens at 20% per annum

Yesterday's market situation, observed in the market, was very bleak, and the market price felt weak and unbearable. Although the interbank lending rate was the same for the morning and afternoon markets at 20% per annum, similar to the previous day, the internal details were very soft, fearing that it would soon have to decline without any possibility of recovery. The additional interest rate for overnight loans initially had 50% to 60% per annum, and the final closing only opened at 10% to 20% per annum, and even sometimes no interest was charged, which was very different from the market at the end of last month. The volume of bills traded in the morning was more than 3.1 million yuan transacted by wire transfer, more than 200,000 yuan in new transactions. The trading volume in the afternoon was more than 400,000 yuan, and the trading volume in the Small General Assembly was more than 300,000 yuan. Bank collections and payments, foreign banks had very little inflow and outflow. Last Month's New Currency Minted 8 Million Yuan

—Factory Contracts 5,150 Contracts—

Central Mint Review Committee Announcement No. 16 states that the 8,005,000 yuan of new coins in the 23rd year submitted by the Central Mint for review in October of this year has been inspected by the 化騐师萬來德 designated by the committee in accordance with the regulations. The fineness and weight are in accordance with the regulations for the manufacture of silver standard currency. It is estimated that 1,610 certificates will be issued, from (23)04914 to (23)06523. In addition, the Class B factory contracts (880 fineness) manufactured by the Central Mint in October, from No. 36318 to No. 41467, a total of 5,150 contracts, were also "supervised and stamped" by 化騐师葛來德 designated by the committee in accordance with the regulations during the "calibration mark," and the fineness and weight of each contract were listed and registered (omitted below).

Major Securities and Bond Market Players Wait and See

—Retail Investors are Silent—

Yesterday, the Chinese Securities Exchange's market fluctuated steadily, and trading became even quieter. Most long and short players are holding a wait-and-see attitude. Major players rarely enter and exit the market. Retail investors' buying and selling are carefully checked. The environment has no favorable changes. The market price is becoming dull. Interbank lending is stable. People's hearts are stable. The future should still have a period of fluctuation. The longer the brewing, the more forceful the 盗勞汉. Once it changes, it should be more intense. Yesterday's process, the first two rounds in the morning, first weak and then strong, only fluctuated by about 5 fen to 1 jiao. The market atmosphere was idle, and everyone seemed to be watching from the sidelines. The afternoon was relatively strong, and the opening continued to be good by 1-2 jiao, which was mostly due to retail investors buying. The closing trading volume was still sparse. The previous series continued to be firm, and the latter series showed slight weakness, but the number was very small, and the overall situation did not deviate from fluctuation. The final market price was slightly better by 5 fen, 1 jiao to 2 jiao or so. After the supervision tax, it was slightly lower, and the trend was not worth mentioning. The total turnover was 7.85 million yuan. 40 shares of the Exchange were listed. The reason for the weakness of the former is not very clear. The latter fell due to poor operating reports. The American rubber industry decided to increase tire prices by 12,000 to 25% from today. However, rubber stocks did not react, and each stock rebounded slightly at the close. It was heard yesterday that a part of the goods had been traded, and the market price rose by about 1 yuan compared to the previous price. However, as the market price rose, sales inevitably became stagnant, as the current market has rebounded by 5-6 yuan compared to the lowest price. It is temporarily 협平.
